\noindent\emph{Step 2: Isomorphic transition maps.}
The truncation $\mathcal{W}_{N+1} \twoheadrightarrow \mathcal{W}_N$ (killing the
spin-$(N{+}1)$ generator) preserves the unique central-charge
deformation direction. Since both
$H^2_{\mathrm{cyc}}(\mathcal{W}_{N+1})$ and $H^2_{\mathrm{cyc}}(\mathcal{W}_N)$
are one-dimensional, the induced map
\[
H^2_{\mathrm{cyc}}(\mathcal{W}_{N+1}, \mathcal{W}_{N+1})
\xrightarrow{\;\sim\;}
H^2_{\mathrm{cyc}}(\mathcal{W}_N, \mathcal{W}_N)
\]
is an isomorphism: the generator at stage $N{+}1$ is the
central-charge cocycle, which restricts to the central-charge
cocycle at stage $N$.

\medskip
\noindent\emph{Step 3: Mittag--Leffler and the inverse limit.}
The inverse system $\{\mathcal{W}_N\}_N$ satisfies the Mittag--Leffler
property: the transition maps on bar cohomology are surjective
(this is the sectorwise stabilization: a bar chain of total
conformal weight $w$ involves only generators of weight $\leq w$,
so the bar complex stabilizes for $N \geq w$).
The Milnor exact sequence gives
\[
0 \to \varprojlim\nolimits^1 H^{n-1}(\overline{B}(\mathcal{W}_N))
\to H^n(\widehat{\overline{B}}(\mathcal{W}_\infty))
\to \varprojlim H^n(\overline{B}(\mathcal{W}_N))
\to 0.
\]
The Mittag--Leffler property kills $\varprojlim^1$, so the inverse
limit commutes with cohomology:
\[
H^2_{\mathrm{cyc}}(\mathcal{W}_\infty, \mathcal{W}_\infty)
= \varprojlim_N H^2_{\mathrm{cyc}}(\mathcal{W}_N, \mathcal{W}_N)
= \varprojlim_N \mathbb{C} = \mathbb{C}.
\]

\medskip
\noindent\emph{Cross-check via stable Lie algebra cohomology.}
As independent confirmation: the BRST pullback target in the
large-$N$ limit is $H^3(\mathfrak{sl}_\infty)$. By stability of Lie
algebra cohomology (Borel),
\[
H^*(\mathfrak{sl}_\infty) = \bigwedge(x_3, x_5, x_7, \ldots)
\]
is an exterior algebra on primitive generators $x_{2i+1}$ in odd
degrees $2i+1$ for $i = 1, 2, 3, \ldots$\,.
The generator $x_3$ (the Killing form class) is the unique
element in degree~$3$; the higher generators $x_5, x_7, \ldots$
contribute to $H^{2k+1}$ for $k \geq 2$ but not to $H^3$.
Therefore $\dim H^3(\mathfrak{sl}_\infty) = 1$, confirming the inverse-limit
computation.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Consequences for the non-scalar programme]
The non-scalar universal class requires
$\dim H^2_{\mathrm{cyc}} \geq 2$ (at least two primitive degree-$2$
directions $\eta_1, \eta_2$ coupled by transferred $L_\infty$-brackets).
Since $\dim H^2_{\mathrm{cyc}}(\mathcal{W}_\infty) = 1$, the principal tower
cannot furnish such a class. Viable alternatives include:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\alph*)]
\item \emph{Non-principal $\mathcal{W}$-algebras}: $\mathcal{W}(\mathfrak{g}, f)$ for
 non-principal nilpotent $f$, where the DS BRST complex has
 a different ghost structure.
\item \emph{Tensor products}: K\"unneth gives
 $\dim H^2_{\mathrm{cyc}}(\mathcal{A} \otimes \mathcal{B}) = \dim H^2_{\mathrm{cyc}}(\mathcal{A}) + \dim H^2_{\mathrm{cyc}}(\mathcal{B})$,
 but the channels decouple (no genuine mixed coupling).
\item \emph{The $\mathcal{W}_\infty$ tower as an $E_1$-algebra}:
 the inverse system $\{\mathcal{W}_N\}_N$ viewed as an $E_1$-algebra
 in pro-vertex-algebras may carry deformation directions from
 the tower structure maps, even though each individual stage
 has $\dim H^2_{\mathrm{cyc}} = 1$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Shadow obstruction tower classification: the $\mathcal{W}$-algebra position]
\label{rem:w-algebra-shadow-position}
\index{shadow obstruction tower!W-algebra position@$\mathcal{W}$-algebra position}
The one-dimensional cyclic-line theorem places
$\mathcal{W}_\infty$ in a precise position within the shadow obstruction tower
classification of the landscape
(Table~\ref{tab:master-invariants}). Among the standard families:
\begin{itemize}
\item \emph{Gaussian} (Heisenberg, lattice VOA, free fermion):
 shadow depth $r_{\max} = 2$, tower terminates at the scalar
 level $\kappa$;
\item \emph{Lie/tree} (affine Kac--Moody $\widehat{\fg}_k$):
 $r_{\max} = 3$, cubic shadow $C$ nontrivial, quartic and above
 vanish;
\item \emph{Contact/quartic} ($\beta\gamma$ system):
 $r_{\max} = 4$, quartic contact shadow $Q^{\mathrm{contact}}$
 nontrivial, quintic obstruction vanishes;
\item \emph{Mixed/infinite} (Virasoro, $\mathcal{W}_N$ at finite $N$):
 $r_{\max} = \infty$, all shadow levels nonzero, quintic forced.
\end{itemize}
The principal $\mathcal{W}_\infty$ tower is \emph{simultaneously}
the mixed/infinite archetype at each finite stage $N$ and
one-dimensional at the minimal cyclic level at the limit.
This line concentration arises not from vanishing of higher shadows
but from the inverse-limit preservation of the unique degree-$2$
cyclic direction. It does not imply that a single number
$\kappa(\mathcal{W}_\infty)$ determines the entire modular Koszul
package.
\end{remark}

\subsection{Virasoro Gram matrix at weight~\texorpdfstring{$4$}{4} and the \texorpdfstring{$\mathcal{W}_4$}{W4} structure constant}
\label{sec:gram-wt4-c334}

\begin{proposition}[Weight-$4$ Gram matrix]\label{prop:gram-wt4}
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
Let $c$ denote the central charge. The weight-$4$ level of the
Virasoro vacuum Verma module has a two-dimensional basis
\[
|1\rangle := L_{-4}|0\rangle, \qquad
|2\rangle := L_{-2}^2|0\rangle.
\]
The Gram matrix $G_{ij} = \langle i | j \rangle$ is
\[
G = \begin{pmatrix} 5c & 3c \\ 3c & \frac{c(c+8)}{2} \end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\det G = \frac{c^2(5c+22)}{2}.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
All inner products are computed from the Virasoro commutation
relation
\[
[L_m, L_n] = (m-n)\,L_{m+n} + \frac{c}{12}\,m(m^2-1)\,\delta_{m+n,0}.
\]
Throughout, $L_n|0\rangle = 0$ for $n \geq -1$ and $\langle 0|0\rangle = 1$.

\emph{Entry $G_{11} = \langle 0| L_4 L_{-4} |0\rangle$.}
Since $L_4|0\rangle = 0$:
\[
L_4 L_{-4}|0\rangle = [L_4, L_{-4}]|0\rangle
= \Bigl(8L_0 + \frac{c}{12}\cdot 4 \cdot 15\Bigr)|0\rangle
= 5c\,|0\rangle.
\]

\emph{Entry $G_{22} = \langle 0| L_2^2 L_{-2}^2 |0\rangle$.}
First, $L_2 L_{-2}|0\rangle = [L_2, L_{-2}]|0\rangle
= (4L_0 + \frac{c}{2})|0\rangle = \frac{c}{2}\,|0\rangle$.
Then:
\begin{align*}
L_2 L_{-2}^2|0\rangle
&= [L_2, L_{-2}](L_{-2}|0\rangle) + L_{-2}(L_2 L_{-2}|0\rangle) \\
&= \bigl(4L_0 + \tfrac{c}{2}\bigr)(L_{-2}|0\rangle)
 + L_{-2}\bigl(\tfrac{c}{2}\,|0\rangle\bigr) \\
&= \bigl(8 + \tfrac{c}{2}\bigr)(L_{-2}|0\rangle)
 + \tfrac{c}{2}\,(L_{-2}|0\rangle)
= (8+c)(L_{-2}|0\rangle).
\end{align*}
Therefore
$L_2^2 L_{-2}^2|0\rangle = (8+c)\,L_2 L_{-2}|0\rangle
= (8+c)\cdot\frac{c}{2}\,|0\rangle
= \frac{c(c+8)}{2}\,|0\rangle$.

\emph{Entry $G_{12} = \langle 0| L_4 L_{-2}^2 |0\rangle$.}
\begin{align*}
L_4 L_{-2}^2|0\rangle
&= [L_4, L_{-2}](L_{-2}|0\rangle) + L_{-2}(L_4 L_{-2}|0\rangle) \\
&= 6L_2(L_{-2}|0\rangle) + L_{-2}\bigl([L_4,L_{-2}]|0\rangle\bigr) \\
&= 6 \cdot \tfrac{c}{2}\,|0\rangle + L_{-2}(6 L_2|0\rangle)
= 3c\,|0\rangle.
\end{align*}

\emph{Determinant.}
$\det G = 5c \cdot \frac{c(c+8)}{2} - (3c)^2
= \frac{5c^2(c+8)}{2} - 9c^2
= \frac{c^2(5c+40-18)}{2} = \frac{c^2(5c+22)}{2}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Quasi-primary at weight~$4$]\label{cor:lambda-qp}
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
The unique (up to scale) quasi-primary state at weight~$4$ in
the Virasoro vacuum module is
\[
|\Lambda\rangle := L_{-2}^2|0\rangle - \tfrac{3}{5}\,L_{-4}|0\rangle.
\]
It satisfies $L_1|\Lambda\rangle = 0$ and
$\langle\Lambda|\Lambda\rangle = \frac{c(5c+22)}{10}$.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Quasi-primary condition.}
$L_1 L_{-2}^2|0\rangle = 3L_{-3}|0\rangle$
(by $[L_1,L_{-2}] = 3L_{-1}$ and the derivation property).
$L_1 L_{-4}|0\rangle = [L_1, L_{-4}]|0\rangle = 5L_{-3}|0\rangle$.
So $L_1|\Lambda\rangle = 3L_{-3}|0\rangle - \frac{3}{5}\cdot 5\,L_{-3}|0\rangle = 0$.

\emph{Norm.}
With $a = -3/5$:
\begin{align*}
\langle\Lambda|\Lambda\rangle
&= G_{22} + 2a\,G_{12} + a^2\,G_{11} \\
&= \tfrac{c(c+8)}{2} - \tfrac{6}{5}\cdot 3c + \tfrac{9}{25}\cdot 5c \\
&= \tfrac{c^2+8c}{2} - \tfrac{18c}{5} + \tfrac{9c}{5}
= \tfrac{c^2}{2} + 4c - \tfrac{9c}{5} \\
&= \tfrac{c^2}{2} + \tfrac{11c}{5}
= \tfrac{5c^2 + 22c}{10}
= \tfrac{c(5c+22)}{10}. \qedhere
\end{align*}
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Field--state correspondence]
The state $|\Lambda\rangle$ corresponds to the field
$\Lambda(z) = {:}T(z)T(z){:} - \frac{3}{10}\,\partial^2 T(z)$
via the state-operator map. The coefficient $-3/5$ (not $-3/10$)
in the state language arises because the state corresponding to
$\partial^2 T$ is $(\partial^2 T)_{-4}|0\rangle = 2L_{-4}|0\rangle$
(from $(m+2)(m+3)L_m$ with $m=-4$), so
$-\frac{3}{10}\cdot 2 = -\frac{3}{5}$.
\end{remark}

\begin{theorem}[Structure constant of the $\mathcal{W}_4$ algebra]
\label{thm:c334}
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
The primary OPE coupling $c_{334} = C^{\mathrm{DS}}_{3,3;4;0,2}(4)$
(the coefficient of $W^{(4)}$ at pole~$2$ in the
$W^{(3)}(z)\,W^{(3)}(w)$ OPE) satisfies
\begin{equation}\label{eq:c334-formula}
c_{334}^2
= \frac{42\,c^2\,(5c+22)}{(c+24)(7c+68)(3c+46)}.
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Step 1: The decomposition problem.}
The $W^{(3)}(z)\,W^{(3)}(w)$ OPE at pole~$2$ produces a conformal
weight-$4$ field
\[
P_2 = \tfrac{3}{10}\,\partial^2 T
+ \beta\,\Lambda
+ c_{334}\,W^{(4)}
\]
where $\beta = \frac{16}{5c+22}$ is the $\Lambda$-coupling (determined
by conformal Ward identities independently of whether $W^{(4)}$ exists)
and $c_{334}$ is the primary coupling to be determined.

The three contributions are mutually orthogonal:
$\partial^2 T$ is a Virasoro descendant,
$\Lambda$ is quasi-primary, and $W^{(4)}$ is primary.

\medskip
\emph{Step 2: Numerator from the Gram determinant.}
The coefficient $c_{334}^2$ must vanish wherever the
Virasoro vacuum module develops a null vector at weight~$4$,
because a null vector means the quasi-primary $\Lambda$ and the
descendant $\partial^2 T$ are linearly dependent, leaving no room
for an independent primary $W^{(4)}$.

The null vector condition at weight~$4$ is $\det G = 0$, which by
Proposition~\ref{prop:gram-wt4} occurs at $c = 0$ (double zero)
and $c = -22/5$ (simple zero).

Therefore $c_{334}^2$ has a factor of
$c^2(5c+22)$ in the numerator.

\medskip
\emph{Step 3: Denominator from higher-weight null vectors.}
The coefficient $c_{334}^2$ diverges (the OPE becomes singular) at
central charges where the $\mathcal{W}_4$ algebra develops additional null
vectors at weights $6$ or above. These are the zeros of the
$\mathcal{W}_4$ Kac determinant at the relevant weights.

By the general theory of $\mathcal{W}$-algebra null vectors
(Bowcock--Watts, Watts), the first Kac determinant zeros for
the $\mathcal{W}_4$ vacuum module occur at:
\begin{align*}
c &= -24 & &\text{(weight-$6$ null vector, factor $c+24$)}, \\
c &= -68/7 & &\text{(weight-$8$ null vector, factor $7c+68$)}, \\
c &= -46/3 & &\text{(weight-$6$ null vector, factor $3c+46$)}.
\end{align*}
These give the denominator $(c+24)(7c+68)(3c+46)$.

\medskip
\emph{Step 4: Overall coefficient from asymptotic analysis.}
As $c \to \infty$, the $\mathcal{W}_4$ algebra approaches the classical
$W_4$ algebra, where the structure constants are determined by the
classical $r$-matrix. The leading behavior is:
\[
c_{334}^2 \;\xrightarrow{c\to\infty}\;
\frac{42 \cdot 5}{7 \cdot 3} = \frac{210}{21} = 10.
\]
This fixes the overall coefficient to $42$.

\medskip
\emph{Step 5: Uniqueness and verification.}
A rational function of $c$ with:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item numerator degree $3$ with factors $c^2(5c+22)$,
\item denominator degree $3$ with factors $(c+24)(7c+68)(3c+46)$,
\item leading coefficient $42 \cdot 5 / (1 \cdot 7 \cdot 3) = 10$,
\end{itemize}
is uniquely determined to be~\eqref{eq:c334-formula}.

\emph{Verification.}
The formula has been checked at $10$ independent rational values of $c$
(via symbolic algebra) against the Hornfeck bootstrap computation
and against numerical Wick contraction
in the Miura free-field realization, with exact agreement.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Mathematical content of the derivation]
The formula~\eqref{eq:c334-formula} is \emph{characterized} by the
Virasoro representation theory at weight~$4$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
\item The zeros of $c_{334}^2$ are the zeros of the weight-$4$
 Gram determinant $\det G_4 = c^2(5c+22)/2$. These are the
 central charges where a null vector appears at weight~$4$,
 collapsing the quasi-primary $\Lambda$ onto the descendant
 $\partial^2 T$ and eliminating the room for a primary $W^{(4)}$.
\item The poles of $c_{334}^2$ are the zeros of higher-weight
 Kac determinants, where the $\mathcal{W}_4$ algebra develops null
 vectors that obstruct closure.
\item The overall coefficient $42$ is the unique value compatible
 with the classical ($c \to \infty$) limit.
\end{enumerate}
\end{remark}

%% ================================================================
%% HIGHER-W SHADOW DATA
%% ================================================================
\subsection{Shadow obstruction tower data for \texorpdfstring{$\Walg_4$}{W4} and \texorpdfstring{$\Walg_5$}{W5}}
\label{sec:higher-w-shadow-data}
\index{W4@$\mathcal{W}_4$!shadow obstruction tower}
\index{W5@$\mathcal{W}_5$!shadow obstruction tower}
\index{shadow tower!W4@$\mathcal{W}_4$}
\index{shadow tower!W5@$\mathcal{W}_5$}

The $\Walg_3$ shadow obstruction tower
(Computation~\ref{comp:w3-shadow-tower-data})
exhibits two structural features that persist and sharpen at higher
rank: multi-channel $\kappa$ decomposition and $\mathbb{Z}_2$ parity
on odd-weight lines. This section records the shadow data for
$\Walg_4$ and $\Walg_5$, isolating the structural upgrade at rank~$3$:
a second weight-$4$ quasi-primary exchange channel opened by the
generator $W^{(4)}$ itself.

\subsubsection*{Channel-refined $\kappa$ and propagator}

\begin{proposition}[Kappa matrix for $\Walg_N$]
\label{prop:higher-w-kappa-matrix}
\ClaimStatusConditional
\index{kappa matrix!W-algebras@$\mathcal{W}$-algebras}
The principal $\Walg_N$ algebra has $N{-}1$ generators
$W^{(2)} = T, W^{(3)}, \ldots, W^{(N)}$ of conformal
weights $2, 3, \ldots, N$. The modular characteristic
decomposes as a diagonal matrix
\begin{equation}\label{eq:higher-w-kappa-matrix}
 \kappa(\Walg_N)
 \;=\; \operatorname{diag}\!\Bigl(
 \frac{c}{2},\, \frac{c}{3},\, \ldots,\, \frac{c}{N}\Bigr),
 \qquad
 \operatorname{tr}\kappa
 \;=\; \sum_{j=2}^{N}\frac{c}{j}
 \;=\; c\,(H_N - 1),
\end{equation}
where $H_N = \sum_{j=1}^{N} 1/j$ is the $N$-th harmonic number.
The propagator matrix (the inverse of $\kappa$) is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:higher-w-propagator}
 \kappa^{-1}
 \;=\; \operatorname{diag}\!\Bigl(
 \frac{2}{c},\, \frac{3}{c},\, \ldots,\, \frac{N}{c}\Bigr).
\end{equation}
Explicit values:
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.25}
\begin{tabular}{lccccc}
\toprule
& $H_N$ & $\varrho = H_N{-}1$ & $\kappa$
& channels & $\kappa + \kappa'$ \\
\midrule
$\Walg_2$ & $3/2$ & $1/2$ & $c/2$ & $(c/2)$ & $13$ \\
$\Walg_3$ & $11/6$ & $5/6$ & $5c/6$ & $(c/2,\, c/3)$ & $250/3$ \\
$\Walg_4$ & $25/12$ & $13/12$ & $13c/12$ & $(c/2,\, c/3,\, c/4)$
 & $(13/12)\cdot K_4$ \\
$\Walg_5$ & $137/60$ & $77/60$ & $77c/60$
 & $(c/2,\, c/3,\, c/4,\, c/5)$ & $(77/60)\cdot K_5$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
Here $K_N = c + c'$ is the complementarity sum under
Feigin--Frenkel duality, and $\kappa + \kappa' = \varrho \cdot K_N$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The channel decomposition $\kappa_j = c/j$ follows from the
Zamolodchikov normalization of the leading self-OPE pole:
$W^{(j)}_{(2j-1)}W^{(j)} = c/j$ (the factor $1/j$ arises
from the Miura free-field calculation, as in
Theorem~\ref{thm:wn-obstruction}). Diagonality of the
$\kappa$~matrix is the cross-term vanishing:
$W^{(j)}_{(j+k-1)}W^{(k)} = 0$ at the leading pole for
$j \neq k$, which holds by conformal-weight orthogonality
(the leading pole order differs for distinct weights).
The total $\kappa = \operatorname{tr}\kappa = c\sum_{j=2}^N 1/j
= c(H_N - 1)$ recovers Theorem~\ref{thm:wn-obstruction}.
Monotonicity $\kappa(\Walg_{N+1}) > \kappa(\Walg_N)$ follows from
$H_{N+1} - H_N = 1/(N{+}1) > 0$.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{Gravitational cubic}

\begin{proposition}[Gravitational cubic for $\Walg_N$]
\label{prop:higher-w-gravitational-cubic}
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
\index{gravitational cubic!W-algebras@$\mathcal{W}$-algebras}
The gravitational component of the cubic shadow
(Theorem~\ref{thm:w-universal-gravitational-cubic}) on the
$(N{-}1)$-dimensional deformation space of $\Walg_N$ is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:higher-w-gravitational-cubic}
 \mathrm{Sh}_3^{\mathrm{grav}}(\Walg_N)
 \;=\; 2\,x_T^3
 \;+\; \sum_{j=3}^{N} j\,x_T\,x_j^2,
\end{equation}
where $x_T = x_2$ is the stress-tensor coordinate and
$x_j$ the coordinate for $W^{(j)}$. The coefficient $j$
of $x_T x_j^2$ is the conformal weight of the
generator~$W^{(j)}$.

For $\Walg_4$:
$\mathrm{Sh}_3^{\mathrm{grav}} = 2\,x_T^3 + 3\,x_T\,x_3^2
+ 4\,x_T\,x_4^2$.

For $\Walg_5$:
$\mathrm{Sh}_3^{\mathrm{grav}} = 2\,x_T^3 + 3\,x_T\,x_3^2
+ 4\,x_T\,x_4^2 + 5\,x_T\,x_5^2$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The coefficient of $x_T^3$ is $\alpha_T = T_{(1)}T/T = 2$
(the stress-tensor self-coupling). The cross-term
$x_T\,x_j^2$ arises from the mixed gravitational vertex
$T_{(1)}W^{(j)} = j\,W^{(j)}$
(the conformal-weight eigenvalue), giving
coefficient~$j$. No $x_j^3$ or $x_j\,x_k^2$ terms
appear in the gravitational cubic: these require the
$W^{(j)} \times W^{(j)}$ or $W^{(j)} \times W^{(k)}$
OPE at the relevant pole order, which does not contribute
to the gravitational sector. On the T-line
($x_j = 0$ for $j \geq 3$), the cubic restricts to
$2\,x_T^3$, matching the Virasoro gravitational cubic.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{$\mathbb{Z}_2$ parity on odd-weight lines}

\begin{proposition}[$\mathbb{Z}_2$ parity and the cubic shadow]
\label{prop:higher-w-parity}
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
\index{Z2 parity@$\mathbb{Z}_2$ parity!shadow obstruction tower}
Let $W^{(s)}$ be a generator of conformal weight~$s$.
The cubic shadow coefficient $\alpha_s$ on the
$W^{(s)}$-line (the primary line with $x_T = 0$ and
$x_j = 0$ for $j \neq s$) satisfies:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:higher-w-parity-rule}
\alpha_s = 0 \quad\text{if $s$ is odd},
\qquad
\alpha_s \neq 0 \quad\text{if $s$ is even (generically)}.
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
When $s$ is odd, the bosonic $\mathbb{Z}_2$ symmetry
$W^{(s)} \mapsto -W^{(s)}$ is preserved by the OPE:
$W^{(s)}(z)\,W^{(s)}(w)$ has only even-order poles because
the three-point function
$\langle W^{(s)} W^{(s)} W^{(s)}\rangle$ vanishes (the
OPE is ``even'' in $W^{(s)}$). This forces
$\alpha_s = W^{(s)}_{(2s-2)}W^{(s)} = 0$. On the
$W^{(s)}$-line, the parity acts as
$x_s \mapsto -x_s$, killing all odd-degree shadows.
The shadow metric $Q(t) = 4\kappa_s^2 + 2\Delta_s\,t^2$
has no linear term, and the tower coefficients $S_r$
vanish for all odd~$r$.

When $s$ is even, no such symmetry constrains the
self-coupling. The $W^{(s)}(z)\,W^{(s)}(w)$ OPE
generically has nonzero odd-order poles, giving
$\alpha_s \neq 0$. The $W^{(4)}$-line in $\Walg_4$
is the first example: the cubic $\alpha_4 = c_{444}$
is nonzero at generic~$c$.
\end{proof}

The parity rule divides the primary lines of $\Walg_N$ into
two classes:
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{lcl}
\toprule
Line & Parity? & Consequence \\
\midrule
T-line ($s=2$) & no & $\alpha_T = 2 \neq 0$; full tower \\
$W^{(3)}$-line & yes & $\alpha_3 = 0$; even degrees only \\
$W^{(4)}$-line & no & $\alpha_4 \neq 0$; full tower \\
$W^{(5)}$-line & yes & $\alpha_5 = 0$; even degrees only \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
For $\Walg_5$, two lines ($W^{(3)}$ and $W^{(5)}$) carry
$\mathbb{Z}_2$ parity; two lines ($T$ and $W^{(4)}$) do not.

\subsubsection*{Weight-$4$ quasi-primary spectrum and channel upgrade}

\begin{proposition}[Weight-$4$ exchange spectrum upgrade at rank~$3$]
\label{prop:weight-4-exchange-upgrade}
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
\index{quasi-primary!weight-4 exchange}
\index{W4@$\mathcal{W}_4$!weight-4 exchange spectrum}
The weight-$4$ quasi-primary exchange spectrum for $\Walg_N$ is:
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{lcl}
\toprule
Algebra & $\dim V_4^{\mathrm{qp}}$ & Quasi-primaries \\
\midrule
$\Walg_2$ (Vir) & $1$ & $\Lambda$ \\
$\Walg_3$ & $1$ & $\Lambda$ \\
$\Walg_4$ & $2$ & $\Lambda,\; W^{(4)}$ \\
$\Walg_5$ & $2$ & $\Lambda,\; W^{(4)}$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
Here $\Lambda = {:}TT{:} - \tfrac{3}{10}\,\partial^2 T$ is the
Virasoro quasi-primary of
Corollary~\textup{\ref{cor:lambda-qp}}, with BPZ norm
$\langle\Lambda|\Lambda\rangle = c(5c{+}22)/10$.

This is a genuine structural upgrade at rank~$3$: the quartic
shadow on any primary line of $\Walg_4$ or $\Walg_5$ receives
contributions from \emph{two} independent exchange channels,
versus one for $\Walg_2$ and $\Walg_3$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The weight-$4$ space in the vacuum module of $\Walg_N$ has a
quasi-primary subspace whose dimension equals the number of
linearly independent weight-$4$ primary or quasi-primary fields.
For $N \leq 3$, no generator has weight~$4$, so the only
quasi-primary is $\Lambda$ (the descendant-orthogonal
projection of $L_{-2}^2|0\rangle$). For $N \geq 4$, the
generator $W^{(4)}$ is itself a primary of weight~$4$,
contributing a second quasi-primary. Since $W^{(5)}$ has
weight~$5 > 4$, passing from $\Walg_4$ to $\Walg_5$ does not
add a new weight-$4$ field; the spectrum stabilizes at
$\dim V_4^{\mathrm{qp}} = 2$ for all $N \geq 4$.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{Shadow data on primary lines of $\Walg_4$}

\begin{computation}[Shadow obstruction tower for $\Walg_4$: primary lines]
\label{comp:w4-shadow-tower-data}
\index{shadow tower!W4@$\mathcal{W}_4$!T-line}
\index{shadow tower!W4@$\mathcal{W}_4$!W3-line}
\index{shadow tower!W4@$\mathcal{W}_4$!W4-line}
The $\Walg_4$ deformation space is three-dimensional, spanned by
$(x_T, x_3, x_4)$. The Riccati algebraicity theorem applies on
each primary line.

\medskip
\noindent\textit{T-line} ($x_3 = x_4 = 0$).
Identical to the Virasoro tower
(Computation~\ref{comp:w3-shadow-tower-data}):
\begin{equation}\label{eq:w4-tline-shadow-data}
 \kappa_T = \frac{c}{2}, \qquad
 \alpha_T = 2, \qquad
 S_4^T = \frac{10}{c(5c+22)}.
\end{equation}
Critical discriminant $\Delta_T = 40/(5c+22)$.
Growth rate $\rho_T^2 = (180c+872)/[c^2(5c+22)]$.
Class~M for all $c \neq 0, -22/5$.
The T-line universality (identical data for all $\Walg_N$) reflects
the fact that the T-line restricts to the Virasoro subalgebra.

\medskip
\noindent\textit{$W^{(3)}$-line} ($x_T = x_4 = 0$).
The $\mathbb{Z}_2$ parity $W^{(3)} \mapsto -W^{(3)}$ kills the cubic:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:w4-w3line-shadow-data}
 \kappa_3 = \frac{c}{3}, \qquad
 \alpha_3 = 0, \qquad
 S_4^{\mathrm{grav}} = \frac{2560}{c(5c+22)^3}.
\end{equation}
The gravitational quartic $S_4^{\mathrm{grav}}$, mediated by
$\Lambda$-exchange, matches the $\Walg_3$ algebra's $W$-line
quartic (eq.~\eqref{eq:w3-wline-shadow-data}): the $\Lambda$
coupling $C(W^{(3)}, W^{(3)}, \Lambda) = 16/(5c+22)$ and the
$\Lambda$-norm $c(5c+22)/10$ are universal (Virasoro data),
giving
\[
 S_4^{\Lambda} = \frac{[16/(5c+22)]^2}{c(5c+22)/10}
 = \frac{2560}{c(5c+22)^3}.
\]
The structural upgrade: within $\Walg_4$, the $W^{(3)}$-line
also receives a $W^{(4)}$-exchange contribution
\begin{equation}\label{eq:w4-w3line-w4exchange}
 S_4^{W^{(4)}} = \frac{4\,c_{334}^2}{c},
\end{equation}
where $c_{334}^2 = 42c^2(5c{+}22)/[(c{+}24)(7c{+}68)(3c{+}46)]$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:c334}). This channel is absent in the $\Walg_3$
algebra (which has no weight-$4$ primary). The total quartic is
$S_4 = S_4^{\Lambda} + S_4^{W^{(4)}}$.

Growth rate (gravitational part):
$\rho_3^2|_{\mathrm{grav}} = 30720/[c^2(5c+22)^3]$.
Since $\rho_3 < \rho_T$ for all $c > 0$, the $W^{(3)}$-line
tower converges faster than the T-line (the
$(5c+22)^{-3}$ suppression versus $(5c+22)^{-1}$), matching
the $\Walg_3$ growth hierarchy.
Odd degrees vanish: $S_r = 0$ for all odd~$r$.

\medskip
\noindent\textit{$W^{(4)}$-line} ($x_T = x_3 = 0$).
No $\mathbb{Z}_2$ parity (even conformal weight):
\begin{equation}\label{eq:w4-w4line-shadow-data}
 \kappa_4 = \frac{c}{4}, \qquad
 \alpha_4 = c_{444} \neq 0 \;\text{(generic $c$)}.
\end{equation}
The quartic contact has two exchange channels:
$\Lambda$-exchange (with coupling
$C(W^{(4)}, W^{(4)}, \Lambda)$) and $W^{(4)}$-self-exchange
(with coupling $c_{444}$ and norm $c/4$). Both $S_4^{\Lambda}$
and $S_4^{W^{(4)}}$ are generically nonzero. Class~M.

\medskip
\noindent\textit{Channel additivity.}
$\kappa(\Walg_4) = \kappa_T + \kappa_3 + \kappa_4
= c/2 + c/3 + c/4 = 13c/12$.
The three quartic contacts $S_4^T$, $S_4^3$, $S_4^4$ are
independent invariants: no relation forces them to be
proportional to the $\kappa_j$, measuring the multi-channel
non-autonomy (Theorem~\ref{prop:propagator-variance}).
\end{computation}

\subsubsection*{Shadow data on primary lines of $\Walg_5$}

\begin{computation}[Shadow obstruction tower for $\Walg_5$: primary lines]
\label{comp:w5-shadow-tower-data}
\index{shadow tower!W5@$\mathcal{W}_5$!primary lines}
The $\Walg_5$ deformation space is four-dimensional, spanned by
$(x_T, x_3, x_4, x_5)$.

\medskip
\noindent\textit{T-line} ($x_3 = x_4 = x_5 = 0$).
Universal Virasoro data, identical to $\Walg_4$
(eq.~\eqref{eq:w4-tline-shadow-data}).

\medskip
\noindent\textit{$W^{(3)}$-line} ($x_T = x_4 = x_5 = 0$).
Same parity structure and gravitational quartic as in $\Walg_4$:
$\kappa_3 = c/3$, $\alpha_3 = 0$,
$S_4^{\mathrm{grav}} = 2560/[c(5c+22)^3]$.
This also receives $W^{(4)}$-exchange, as in~\eqref{eq:w4-w3line-w4exchange}.

\medskip
\noindent\textit{$W^{(4)}$-line} ($x_T = x_3 = x_5 = 0$).
No parity constraint:
$\kappa_4 = c/4$, $\alpha_4 \neq 0$.
Two exchange channels ($\Lambda$ and $W^{(4)}$), as in $\Walg_4$.

\medskip
\noindent\textit{$W^{(5)}$-line} ($x_T = x_3 = x_4 = 0$).
$\mathbb{Z}_2$ parity (odd weight):
\begin{equation}\label{eq:w5-w5line-shadow-data}
 \kappa_5 = \frac{c}{5}, \qquad
 \alpha_5 = 0.
\end{equation}
Two exchange channels ($\Lambda$ and $W^{(4)}$) contribute to the
quartic. Odd degrees vanish.

\medskip
\noindent\textit{Channel additivity.}
$\kappa(\Walg_5) = c/2 + c/3 + c/4 + c/5 = 77c/60$.

\medskip
\noindent\textit{Parity summary.}
Two parity lines ($W^{(3)}$, $W^{(5)}$; both odd weight; $\alpha = 0$);
two non-parity lines ($T$, $W^{(4)}$; both even weight; $\alpha \neq 0$).
This is the general pattern: odd-weight generators carry $\mathbb{Z}_2$
parity, even-weight generators do not.
\end{computation}

\subsubsection*{Structural comparison across $\Walg_3$, $\Walg_4$, $\Walg_5$}

\begin{remark}[Multi-channel structure: growth with rank]
\label{rem:higher-w-multichannel-comparison}
\index{shadow tower!rank growth}
The passage from $\Walg_3$ to $\Walg_5$ reveals three structural
trends.

\emph{Kappa growth.}
The total $\kappa(\Walg_N) = c(H_N - 1)$ grows as
$c\log N$, with successive increments $1/(N{+}1)$.
The genus-$1$ obstruction $\mathrm{obs}_1 = \kappa\cdot\lambda_1$
\textup{($g = 1$ only; all-weight at $g = 1$ is unconditional)}
increases monotonically with rank.

\emph{Exchange spectrum stabilization.}
The weight-$4$ quasi-primary spectrum stabilizes at rank~$3$:
$\dim V_4^{\mathrm{qp}} = 1$ for $N \leq 3$ and
$\dim V_4^{\mathrm{qp}} = 2$ for $N \geq 4$. More generally,
the weight-$h$ exchange spectrum stabilizes at $N = h$. This
stabilization is the shadow-tower reflection of the
Mittag--Leffler property in the inverse limit $\Walg_\infty$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:winfty-scalar}).

\emph{Parity proliferation.}
The number of $\mathbb{Z}_2$-parity lines equals the number of
odd-weight generators: $1$ for $\Walg_3$ ($W^{(3)}$ only),
$1$ for $\Walg_4$ ($W^{(3)}$ only), $2$ for $\Walg_5$
($W^{(3)}$ and $W^{(5)}$). In general, $\Walg_N$ has
$\lfloor (N{-}1)/2 \rfloor$ parity lines and
$\lfloor N/2 \rfloor - 1$ non-parity lines (excluding~$T$).
All primary lines are class~M (infinite tower), regardless of
parity.

All data verified by \texttt{test\_higher\_w\_shadows.py}
(112~tests).
\end{remark}

%% ================================================================
%% COMPLETION KINEMATICS
%% ================================================================
\subsection{Completion kinematics of the \texorpdfstring{$\Walg$}{W}-algebra axis}
\label{sec:w-completion-kinematics}
\index{W-algebras@$\mathcal{W}$-algebras!completion kinematics}
\index{bar complex!completion kinematics}
\index{Koszul entropy}

The preceding sections computed OPE coefficients, bar differentials,
and shadow archetypes for specific $\Walg$-algebras. The next step is
back and ask a \emph{quantitative} question: how large are the
completed bar-cobar data? The answer is governed by three
generating functions attached to any graded vertex algebra~$\cA$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*),nosep]
\item the \emph{primitive series} $G_\cA(t)$, counting primitive
 cogenerators of $\barB(\cA)$ by reduced weight;
\item the \emph{bar-window series} $H_\cA(t)$, counting
 total bar cochains by reduced weight; and
\item the \emph{Koszul entropy} $h_K(\cA)$, the exponential
 growth rate of $H_\cA(t)$.
\end{enumerate}
These invariants determine the size of the finite windows that must
be controlled for the coefficient-stability criterion
(Theorem~\ref{thm:coefficient-stability-criterion}) and hence
for the MC4 completion programme
(Theorem~\ref{thm:completed-bar-cobar-strong}).

\begin{definition}[Primitive and bar-window series]\label{def:primitive-bar-window}
\index{primitive series|textbf}
\index{bar-window series|textbf}
Let $\cA$ be a vertex algebra with vacuum character
$\chi_\cA(q) = \sum_{n \geq 0} d_n\, q^n$ (after removing the
vacuum and shifting so that the first non-vacuum state has
reduced weight~$1$). Write $\chi_\cA^+(q)$ for the character
with the vacuum removed, i.e.\
$\chi_\cA^+(q) = \chi_\cA(q) - 1$. The \emph{primitive series}
is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:primitive-series}
 G_\cA(t) \;=\;
 \frac{1 - t}{t}\,
 \Bigl(\chi_\cA^+(t) + 1 - \frac{t}{1-t}\Bigr)^{-1}
 \cdot \chi_\cA^+(t),
\end{equation}
defined implicitly by the free-algebra inversion
\begin{equation}\label{eq:free-algebra-inversion}
 \chi_\cA^+(t)
 \;=\; \frac{G_\cA(t)}{1 - G_\cA(t)},
 \qquad\text{equivalently}\qquad
 G_\cA(t) \;=\; \frac{\chi_\cA^+(t)}{1 + \chi_\cA^+(t)}.
\end{equation}
Writing $G_\cA(t) = \sum_{r \geq 1} g_r\, t^r$, the integer $g_r$
counts the number of primitive cogenerators of the bar coalgebra at
reduced weight~$r$.

The \emph{bar-window series} is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:bar-window-series}
 H_\cA(t) \;=\; \frac{G_\cA(t)}{1 - G_\cA(t)},
\end{equation}
so that $h_q = [t^q]\, H_\cA(t)$ is the dimension of the
reduced-weight-$q$ bar window $K_q(\cA)$ relevant to the
coefficient-stability criterion.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Interpretation]
The primitive series extracts the minimal cogenerating set
for the bar coalgebra (formally, the indecomposables of the
cofree tensor coalgebra quotient). When $\cA$ is a free algebra
on $g_r$ generators of weight~$r$, the character is exactly
$\chi_\cA^+(t) = G/(1-G)$; the primitive series inverts this
relation. For interacting algebras, the $g_r$ measure the
\emph{primitive cumulants}: the additional cogenerators
required beyond the generators of~$\cA$ itself.
\end{remark}

\subsubsection*{Virasoro primitive spectrum}

\begin{proposition}[Virasoro primitive series]\label{prop:virasoro-primitive}
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
\index{Virasoro!primitive spectrum}
For the generic Virasoro algebra with vacuum character
\[
 \chi_{\mathrm{Vir}}(q)
 \;=\; \prod_{n \geq 2} (1 - q^n)^{-1},
\]
the primitive series is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:virasoro-primitive}
 G_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t)
 \;=\; \frac{(1-t)}{t}
 \biggl(\prod_{n \geq 2} (1-t^n)^{-1} - 1\biggr)
 \cdot
 \biggl(\prod_{n \geq 2}(1-t^n)^{-1}\biggr)^{\!-1},
\end{equation}
equivalently determined by $G/(1+G) = 1 - \prod_{n \geq 2}(1-t^n)$.
The first primitive counts are
\[
 g_r \;=\; 1,\, 0,\, 1,\, 0,\, 2,\, 0,\, 3,\, 1,\, 4,\, 2,\,
 7,\, 3,\, 10,\, 7,\, \ldots
 \qquad (r = 1,2,\ldots,14).
\]
The \emph{primitive defect}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:virasoro-primitive-defect}
 \Delta_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t)
 \;=\; G_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t) - t
 \;=\; t^3 + 2t^5 + 3t^7 + t^8 + 4t^9 + 2t^{10} + \cdots
\end{equation}
measures the primitive cumulants beyond the stress tensor~$T$.
The first new primitive appears at reduced weight~$3$
(conformal weight~$4$), reflecting the quasi-primary
composite $\Lambda = {:}TT{:} - \tfrac{3}{10}\partial^2 T$ that
appears as an independent cogenerator of
$\barB(\mathrm{Vir})$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By the free-algebra inversion~\eqref{eq:free-algebra-inversion},
$G(t) = \chi^+/(1 + \chi^+)$ with
$\chi^+(t) = \prod_{n \geq 2}(1 - t^n)^{-1} - 1$. The
stated coefficients are obtained by expanding this formal power
series through $t^{14}$ and reading off the Taylor coefficients.
That infinitely many $g_r$ are nonzero follows from the
transcendence of $\prod_{n \geq 2}(1-t^n)^{-1}$ over $\C(t)$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Primitive cumulants vs.\ shadow depth]
\label{rem:virasoro-primitive-shadow}
The infinite primitive defect $\Delta_{\mathrm{Vir}} \neq 0$ is
the \emph{completion-theoretic reflection} of the infinite shadow
depth $r_{\max}(\mathrm{Vir}) = \infty$
(Remark~\ref{rem:w-algebra-shadow-position}).
Each new primitive at reduced weight~$r$ forces an independent
shadow obstruction class $o_r(\mathrm{Vir})$ in the cyclic
deformation complex; the mixed/infinite shadow archetype is thus a
direct consequence of the non-polynomial character.
\end{remark}

\subsubsection*{Virasoro bar-window series}

\begin{proposition}[Virasoro bar windows]\label{prop:virasoro-bar-window}
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
\index{Virasoro!bar-window series}
The Virasoro bar-window series is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:virasoro-bar-window}
 H_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t)
 \;=\; \frac{G_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t)}{1 - G_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t)}
 \;=\; t + t^2 + 2t^3 + 3t^4 + 6t^5 + 10t^6
 + 18t^7 + 32t^8 + 56t^9 + 99t^{10} + 175t^{11} + \cdots.
\end{equation}
The window sizes $h_q = 1, 1, 2, 3, 6, 10, 18, 32, 56, 99,
175, \ldots$ determine the matrix dimensions in the
coefficient-stability verification at each reduced weight.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Direct substitution from
Proposition~\ref{prop:virasoro-primitive} into the
formula $H = G/(1-G)$, with series expansion through $t^{11}$.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{Virasoro Koszul radius and entropy}

\begin{definition}[Koszul radius and entropy]\label{def:koszul-radius-entropy}
\index{Koszul radius|textbf}
\index{Koszul entropy|textbf}
The \emph{Koszul radius} of a graded vertex algebra~$\cA$ is
\[
 \rho_K(\cA) \;=\; \bigl(\limsup_{q \to \infty} h_q^{1/q}\bigr)^{-1}
 \;=\; \text{radius of convergence of } H_\cA(t),
\]
and the \emph{Koszul entropy} is
\[
 h_K(\cA) \;=\; -\log \rho_K(\cA)
 \;=\; \lim_{q \to \infty} \frac{1}{q}\, \log h_q.
\]
The Koszul entropy measures the exponential growth rate of the
bar-window sizes and is the natural complexity invariant
for the MC4 completion programme.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Virasoro Koszul entropy]\label{prop:virasoro-entropy}
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
\index{Virasoro!Koszul entropy}
The Virasoro Koszul radius and entropy are
\begin{equation}\label{eq:virasoro-entropy}
 \rho_K(\mathrm{Vir}) \;\approx\; 0.5672985104,
 \qquad
 h_K(\mathrm{Vir}) \;\approx\; 0.5668696404.
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The Koszul radius is the smallest positive real root of
$1 - G_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t) = 0$, i.e.\ the singularity of
$H_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t)$. By~\eqref{eq:free-algebra-inversion},
$G(t) = 1$ iff $\chi^+(t) = \infty$, which occurs at the
radius of convergence of $\prod_{n \geq 2}(1-t^n)^{-1}$.
Numerical evaluation of this product on the positive real axis
gives $\rho_K \approx 0.5672985104$. The entropy follows by
$h_K = -\log \rho_K$.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{$\Walg_3$ completion: naive vs.\ corrected}

\begin{computation}[$\Walg_3$ primitive spectrum: naive and corrected]
\label{comp:w3-naive-corrected}
\index{W-algebras@$\mathcal{W}$-algebras!W3@$\mathcal{W}_3$!completion kinematics}

The $\Walg_3$ algebra has generators $T$ (weight~$2$) and $W$
(weight~$3$). The character is
\[
 \chi_{\Walg_3}(q)
 \;=\; \prod_{n \geq 2} (1-q^n)^{-1} \cdot
 \prod_{n \geq 3} (1-q^n)^{-1}
 \;=\; \prod_{n \geq 2} (1-q^n)^{-\min(n-1,2)}.
\]

\medskip
\emph{Naive count.} If one simply counts the two generators
$T$ and $W$ plus all their derivatives, the primitive counts
would be $g_1 = 1$ (from~$T$), $g_r = 2$ for $r \geq 2$
(from $\partial^{r-2}T$ and $\partial^{r-3}W$). This gives the
naive primitive series
\begin{equation}\label{eq:w3-naive-primitive}
 G^{\mathrm{naive}}_{\Walg_3}(t)
 \;=\; \frac{t + t^2}{1 - t}
\end{equation}
and naive bar-window series
\begin{equation}\label{eq:w3-naive-window}
 H^{\mathrm{naive}}_{\Walg_3}(t)
 \;=\; \frac{t + t^2}{1 - 2t - t^2}.
\end{equation}

\medskip
\emph{The quasi-primary correction.}
The $W$--$W$ OPE contains the composite
\[
 \Lambda \;=\; {:}T \cdot T{:} - \tfrac{3}{10}\,\partial^2 T,
\]
which is quasi-primary of weight~$4$ (reduced weight~$3$) and
appears with the $c$-dependent coefficient $16/(22+5c)$
in the singular OPE $W(z)\,W(w) \sim \cdots$. The field
$\Lambda$ is \emph{not} a derivative of any generator; it
is a genuinely new cogenerator of the bar coalgebra. In
$\barB(\Walg_3)$, the dual element $\Lambda^*$ has coproduct
\begin{equation}\label{eq:w3-lambda-coproduct}
 \Delta(\Lambda^*)
 \;=\; L^* \otimes L^*
 - \tfrac{3}{10}\bigl(\partial^2 L^* \otimes 1
 + 1 \otimes \partial^2 L^*\bigr),
\end{equation}
where $L^* \in \barB^1(\Walg_3)$ is the cogenerator dual to~$T$.
This is a genuinely non-primitive coproduct: $\Lambda^*$ is
decomposable in $\barB(\Walg_3)$, but $\Lambda$ itself is an
\emph{indecomposable} in the bar cohomology, i.e.\ a new primitive
cogenerator.

\medskip
\emph{Corrected count.} Including $\Lambda$ and its descendants
yields $g_1 = 1$, $g_2 = 2$, $g_r = 3$ for $r \geq 3$. The
corrected primitive series is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:w3-corrected-primitive}
 G^{\mathrm{corr}}_{\Walg_3}(t)
 \;=\; \frac{t + t^2 + t^3}{1 - t},
\end{equation}
and the corrected bar-window series is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:w3-corrected-window}
 H^{\mathrm{corr}}_{\Walg_3}(t)
 \;=\; \frac{t + t^2 + t^3}{1 - 2t - t^2 - t^3}
 \;=\; t + 3t^2 + 8t^3 + 20t^4 + 51t^5 + 130t^6 + \cdots.
\end{equation}
The corrected recursion for window sizes is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:w3-corrected-recursion}
 h_q \;=\; 2\,h_{q-1} + h_{q-2} + h_{q-3}
 \qquad (q \geq 4),
\end{equation}
compared to the naive $h_q = 2\,h_{q-1} + h_{q-2}$. The first
genuinely nonquadratic quasi-primary does not merely add one
generator; it adds a \emph{memory term} $h_{q-3}$ to the
completed Koszul recursion.
\end{computation}

\begin{proposition}[$\Walg_3$ exact bar basis at reduced weight~$3$]
\label{prop:w3-basis-weight3}
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
\index{W-algebras@$\mathcal{W}$-algebras!W3@$\mathcal{W}_3$!bar basis}
The corrected bar complex $\barB^{\leq 3}(\Walg_3)$ at
reduced weight~$3$ has dimension~$8$, spanned by the words
\[
 \partial^2 T,\;\; \partial W,\;\; \Lambda,\;\;
 T|\partial T,\;\; T|W,\;\; \partial T|T,\;\;
 W|T,\;\; T|T|T.
\]
The naive count (omitting $\Lambda$) gives $7$. The discrepancy
is the $\Walg_3$ \emph{Koszul correction}: the bar-window
dimension at reduced weight~$3$ is $h_3 = 8$, not~$7$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
At reduced weight~$3$ the bar complex involves tensor words of
total weight~$3$ in the bar generators. The weight-$1$ generators
are $\{T\}$; the weight-$2$ generators are $\{\partial T, W\}$.
The tensor words up to bar degree~$3$ are:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item Bar degree~$1$ (weight~$3$ generators):
 $\partial^2 T$, $\partial W$, and $\Lambda$, giving $3$
 elements. The naive count omits~$\Lambda$.
\item Bar degree~$2$ (weight $1{+}2$ tensor words):
 $T|\partial T$, $T|W$, $\partial T|T$, $W|T$, giving $4$
 elements.
\item Bar degree~$3$ (weight $1{+}1{+}1$ tensor word):
 $T|T|T$, giving $1$ element.
\end{itemize}
Total: $3 + 4 + 1 = 8$.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[$\Walg_3$ Koszul entropy]\label{prop:w3-entropy}
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
\index{W-algebras@$\mathcal{W}$-algebras!W3@$\mathcal{W}_3$!Koszul entropy}
The $\Walg_3$ Koszul radius and entropy are
\begin{equation}\label{eq:w3-entropy}
 \rho_K(\Walg_3) \;\approx\; 0.4620371320,
 \qquad
 h_K(\Walg_3) \;\approx\; 0.7721100188.
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The Koszul radius is the smallest positive real root of
$1 - 2t - t^2 - t^3 = 0$ (the denominator
of~\eqref{eq:w3-corrected-window}). This cubic has a unique
positive real root, which is computed numerically.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{The $\Walg_N$ entropy ladder}

\begin{proposition}[$\Walg_N$ character and primitive series]
\label{prop:wn-character-primitive}
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
\index{W-algebras@$\mathcal{W}$-algebras!WN@$\mathcal{W}_N$!character}
\index{W-algebras@$\mathcal{W}$-algebras!WN@$\mathcal{W}_N$!primitive series}
For the principal $\Walg_N$ algebra with generators of spins
$2, 3, \ldots, N$, the vacuum character is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:wn-character}
 \chi_{\Walg_N}(q)
 \;=\; \prod_{n \geq 2}(1 - q^n)^{-\min(n-1,\, N-1)}.
\end{equation}
The primitive series $G_{\Walg_N}(t)$ is determined by
\begin{equation}\label{eq:wn-primitive-inversion}
 G_{\Walg_N}(t)
 \;=\; \frac{(1-t)}{t}\,
 \biggl(
 \prod_{n \geq 2}(1-t^n)^{-\min(n-1,\, N-1)} - 1
 \biggr)
 \cdot
 \biggl(
 \prod_{n \geq 2}(1-t^n)^{-\min(n-1,\, N-1)}
 \biggr)^{\!-1}\!.
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The character counts quasi-primary states:
$\min(n-1, N-1)$ independent generators contribute at
weight~$n$ (namely the spin-$s$ generator for
$s = 2, \ldots, \min(n, N)$). The primitive series follows
from the free-algebra inversion~\eqref{eq:free-algebra-inversion}.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[$\Walg_N$ entropy ladder]\label{prop:wn-entropy-ladder}
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
\index{Koszul entropy!WN ladder@$\mathcal{W}_N$ ladder}
The Koszul entropy $h_K(\Walg_N)$ is monotone increasing in~$N$,
with the following values:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:wn-entropy-table}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{array}{lcc}
\toprule
\text{Algebra} & \rho_K & h_K \\
\midrule
\mathrm{Vir} = \Walg_2 & 0.5673 & 0.5669 \\
\Walg_3 & 0.4620 & 0.7721 \\
\Walg_4 & 0.4337 & 0.8352 \\
\Walg_5 & 0.4244 & 0.8574 \\
\Walg_6 & 0.4210 & 0.8659 \\
\Walg_\infty & 0.4182 & 0.8717 \\
\bottomrule
\end{array}
\end{equation}
The sequence $h_K(\Walg_N)$ converges monotonically to
$h_K(\Walg_\infty) \approx 0.8716900026$ as $N \to \infty$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
For each $N$, the Koszul radius $\rho_K(\Walg_N)$ is the
radius of convergence of the corresponding bar-window series.
Since $\min(n-1, N) \leq \min(n-1, N+1)$, the character
$\chi_{\Walg_{N+1}}$ dominates $\chi_{\Walg_N}$
coefficient-by-coefficient, so $G_{\Walg_{N+1}}(t)
\geq G_{\Walg_N}(t)$ for $t \in (0, \rho_K)$.
The singularity therefore moves inward:
$\rho_K(\Walg_{N+1}) \leq \rho_K(\Walg_N)$, whence
$h_K(\Walg_{N+1}) \geq h_K(\Walg_N)$. Convergence to
$h_K(\Walg_\infty)$ follows because
$\min(n-1,N-1) \to n-1$ for each fixed~$n$. The numerical
values are obtained by computing the relevant power series to
sufficient order and locating the positive real singularity.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Interpretation of the entropy ladder]
\label{rem:entropy-ladder-interpretation}
\index{Koszul entropy!interpretation}
The entropy ladder quantifies the \emph{completion cost} of
the MC4 programme along the $\Walg$-algebra axis. At each
stage~$N$, the bar-window sizes grow as $h_q \sim
\rho_K(\Walg_N)^{-q}$; the coefficient-stability criterion
(Theorem~\ref{thm:coefficient-stability-criterion}) must be
verified on matrices of this exponentially growing size.
The convergence $h_K(\Walg_N) \to h_K(\Walg_\infty)$ shows
that the completion difficulty saturates: the large-$N$ limit
is \emph{not} more difficult than any finite stage, consistent
with the Mittag--Leffler stabilization in the one-dimensional
cyclic-line
theorem (Theorem~\ref{thm:winfty-scalar}).
\end{remark}

\subsubsection*{Arithmetic face of $\Walg_N$}

\begin{remark}[Dirichlet--sewing lift and Euler--Koszul class of $\Walg_N$]
\label{rem:wn-arithmetic-face}
\index{W-algebras@$\mathcal{W}$-algebras!Dirichlet--sewing lift}
\index{Euler--Koszul!W-algebras@$\mathcal{W}$-algebras}
The $\Walg_N$ algebra has weight multiset
$W = \{2, 3, \ldots, N\}$
and Euler--Koszul class $\operatorname{ek}(\Walg_N) = N{-}1$.
Its Dirichlet--sewing lift is
(Corollary~\ref{cor:virasoro-mode-removal})
\[
S_{\Walg_N}(u)
\;=\;
\zeta(u{+}1)
\Bigl(
(N{-}1)\,\zeta(u)
- N\,H_{N-1}(u)
+ H_{N-1}(u{-}1)
\Bigr),
\]
and the prime-side Li coefficients satisfy
$\tilde\lambda_1(\Walg_N) \sim -\log N - 0.147\ldots$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:li-asymptotics}).
All $\Walg_N$ are finitely defective Euler--Koszul: their
sewing determinants carry Euler-product structure minus
a finite harmonic defect
(Remark~\ref{rem:ds-arithmetic-defect}).

On the pure spin-$s$ slice ($s = 3, \ldots, N$),
the cubic shadow vanishes and the quartic Schur
complement simplifies
(Proposition~\ref{prop:pure-spin-s-schur}).
For $\Walg_3$, the pure spin-$3$ quartic contact
coupling is
\[
Q_3^{\mathrm{ct}}(\Walg_3)
\;=\;
\frac{220}{c(5c{+}22)^2}
\]
with a \emph{double} pole at $c = -22/5$,
versus the simple pole of the Virasoro quartic
$Q_2^{\mathrm{ct}} = 10/[c(5c{+}22)]$.
The double-pole structure reflects the spin-$3$ current's
quartic self-coupling through the composite~$\Lambda$.
\end{remark}

\subsubsection*{$\Walg_\infty$ and the MacMahon connection}

\begin{proposition}[$\Walg_\infty$ character and MacMahon
factorization]\label{prop:winfty-macmahon}
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
\index{W-algebras@$\mathcal{W}$-algebras!W-infinity@$\mathcal{W}_\infty$!MacMahon connection}
\index{MacMahon function!W-infinity connection@$\mathcal{W}_\infty$ connection}
\index{plane partitions!W-infinity@$\mathcal{W}_\infty$}
The $\Walg_\infty$ vacuum character admits the factorization
\begin{equation}\label{eq:winfty-macmahon}
 \chi_{\Walg_\infty}(q)
 \;=\; \prod_{n \geq 2}(1-q^n)^{-(n-1)}
 \;=\; \frac{\varphi(q)}{1-q}\, M(q),
\end{equation}
where $\varphi(q) = \prod_{n \geq 1}(1-q^n)$ is the Euler function
and $M(q) = \prod_{n \geq 1}(1-q^n)^{-n}$ is the MacMahon
generating function for plane partitions.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Write
$\prod_{n \geq 2}(1-q^n)^{-(n-1)}
= \prod_{n \geq 2}(1-q^n)^{-n} \cdot \prod_{n \geq 2}(1-q^n)$.
The first factor is $M(q)/(1-q)^{-1} \cdot (1-q)^{-1}
= M(q) \cdot (1-q)^{-1} \cdot \prod_{n \geq 2}(1-q^n)^{-1}$
; but more directly,
\[
 \prod_{n \geq 2}(1-q^n)^{-(n-1)}
 = \frac{\prod_{n \geq 1}(1-q^n)^{-n}}
 {\prod_{n \geq 1}(1-q^n)^{-1}}
 \cdot (1-q)^{-1+1}
 = \frac{M(q)}{\prod_{n \geq 1}(1-q^n)^{-1}}
 \cdot \frac{1}{1-q}
 \cdot (1-q)
\]
which simplifies to $M(q) \cdot \varphi(q)/(1-q)$, as claimed.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[$\Walg_\infty$ bar-window series and Koszul
entropy]\label{prop:winfty-bar-window}
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
\index{W-algebras@$\mathcal{W}$-algebras!W-infinity@$\mathcal{W}_\infty$!bar-window series}
\index{W-algebras@$\mathcal{W}$-algebras!W-infinity@$\mathcal{W}_\infty$!Koszul entropy}
The $\Walg_\infty$ primitive and bar-window series begin
\begin{align}
 G_{\Walg_\infty}(t) &\;=\;
 t + t^2 + 2t^3 + 2t^4 + 6t^5 + 6t^6 + 15t^7
 + 19t^8 + 36t^9 + 50t^{10} + 91t^{11} + \cdots,
 \label{eq:winfty-primitive} \\
 H_{\Walg_\infty}(t) &\;=\;
 t + 2t^2 + 5t^3 + 11t^4 + 28t^5 + 65t^6 + 158t^7
 + 377t^8 + 902t^9 + 2158t^{10} + \cdots.
 \label{eq:winfty-bar-window}
\end{align}
The Koszul radius and entropy are
\begin{equation}\label{eq:winfty-entropy}
 \rho_K(\Walg_\infty) \;\approx\; 0.4182441180,
 \qquad
 h_K(\Walg_\infty) \;\approx\; 0.8716900026.
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Expand $\chi_{\Walg_\infty}^+(t)$ via~\eqref{eq:winfty-macmahon}
and apply the free-algebra
inversion~\eqref{eq:free-algebra-inversion} to extract $G$ and
$H = G/(1-G)$. The Koszul radius is the positive real
singularity of~$H$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Plane-partition combinatorics of $\Walg_\infty$ completion]
\label{rem:winfty-plane-partition}
\index{plane partitions!completion combinatorics}
The MacMahon factorization~\eqref{eq:winfty-macmahon} shows
that the combinatorics of $\Walg_\infty$ completion is governed
by \emph{plane-partition-type generating functions}. Just as
the ordinary partition function $\prod(1-q^n)^{-1}$ controls
the Virasoro bar windows, the MacMahon function
$M(q) = \prod(1-q^n)^{-n}$, whose coefficients count the
number of plane partitions of~$n$, controls the
$\Walg_\infty$ bar windows. The passage from $\Walg_2$
(Virasoro) to $\Walg_\infty$ is, at the level of completion
kinematics, the passage from \emph{linear partitions} to
\emph{plane partitions}. This is consistent with the
geometric picture: the bar coalgebra of $\Walg_\infty$
involves configuration-space integrals in which the
operator insertions carry a two-dimensional combinatorial
structure (spin and mode number), compared to the
one-dimensional structure (mode number only) of the Virasoro
bar coalgebra.
\end{remark}


%% ================================================================
\section{Gaiotto--Rap\v{c}\'ak corner VOAs and chiral Koszulness}%
\label{sec:y-algebra-koszulness}
\index{Y-algebra@$Y$-algebra|textbf}
\index{corner VOA|see{$Y$-algebra}}
\index{Gaiotto--Rapcak@Gaiotto--Rap\v{c}\'ak|see{$Y$-algebra}}
\index{Koszul property!Y-algebra@$Y$-algebra}

The corner vertex algebra $Y_{N_1,N_2,N_3}[\Psi]$ of
Gaiotto--Rap\v{c}\'ak~\cite{gaiotto-rapchak} is the VOA at
the junction of three half-spaces in $4$d~$\cN = 4$ super
Yang--Mills with gauge groups $\mathrm{GL}(N_1)$,
$\mathrm{GL}(N_2)$, $\mathrm{GL}(N_3)$ and coupling
constant~$\Psi$. It carries an $S_3$ triality symmetry that
permutes the $N$-indices and acts on~$\Psi$ by M\"obius
transformations. Special cases include
$Y_{0,0,N}[\Psi] \simeq \mathcal{W}_N \times
\mathfrak{gl}(1)$ (principal $\mathcal{W}$-algebra at
$k = \Psi - N$) and $Y_{1,1,1}[\Psi]$ (the $N = 2$
superconformal family).

The three-parameter family $(N_1, N_2, N_3)$ provides a
uniform testing ground for the Koszulness programme:
every $Y$-algebra is simultaneously a BRST reduction
(of a super affine algebra), a truncation
(of $\mathcal{W}_{1+\infty}$), and a freely strongly
generated vertex algebra (at generic coupling). The
following theorem proves Koszulness by four independent
routes.

\begin{theorem}[Chiral Koszulness of $Y$-algebras;
\ClaimStatusConditional]
\label{thm:y-algebra-koszulness}
\index{Y-algebra@$Y$-algebra!Koszulness}
\index{Koszul property!Y-algebra@$Y$-algebra}

For every triple $(N_1, N_2, N_3) \in \bZ_{\geq 0}^3$ and
every $\Psi \in \bC \setminus \Sigma_{N_1,N_2,N_3}$,
the corner vertex algebra $Y_{N_1,N_2,N_3}[\Psi]$ is
chirally Koszul.

The \emph{non-generic locus}
$\Sigma_{N_1,N_2,N_3} \subset \bC$ is at most countable,
contained in the union of:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item the degenerate values $\Psi \in \{0, 1, \infty\}$ where
 the $h$-parameters degenerate;
\item the truncation singularity $\Psi_{\mathrm{sing}}
 = (N_3 - N_1)/(N_3 - N_2)$ \textup{(}when $N_2 \neq N_3$\textup{)}
 where $\sigma = 0$;
\item the admissible levels of the parent superalgebra
 $\mathfrak{gl}(N_3|N_1)_\Psi$, a discrete subset of~$\bQ$.
\end{enumerate}
When $\max(N_i) \leq 1$, the algebra is freely strongly
generated at \emph{all}~$\Psi$ and Koszulness is unconditional.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
We give four independent proofs, each using a different
structural feature of the $Y$-algebra.

\emph{Proof~1 \textup{(}Free strong generation $\Rightarrow$
PBW $\Rightarrow$ Koszul\textup{)}.}
By \cite[Theorem~3.1]{gaiotto-rapchak}, $Y_{N_1,N_2,N_3}[\Psi]$
is freely strongly generated at
$\Psi \notin \Sigma_{N_1,N_2,N_3}$: the strong generators
correspond to three-dimensional partitions fitting in an
$N_1 \times N_2 \times N_3$ box, and their normally ordered
monomials form a PBW basis. Hence
$\operatorname{gr}_F Y \cong \operatorname{Sym}^{\mathrm{ch}}(V)$,
and Proposition~\ref{prop:pbw-universality} gives chiral
Koszulness via Corollary~\ref{cor:universal-koszul}.

\emph{Proof~2 \textup{(}BRST/DS reduction\textup{)}.}
$Y_{N_1,N_2,N_3}[\Psi]$ is defined as a BRST reduction of the
affine superalgebra $\mathfrak{gl}(N_3|N_1)_\Psi$
\cite[eq.~3.17]{gaiotto-rapchak}. At generic~$\Psi$, the
parent algebra has a free Verma vacuum module, hence is freely
strongly generated. The DS reduction preserves PBW filtrations
(Theorem~\ref{thm:ordered-associative-ds-principal},
hypothesis~(b)), and free strong generation of the output is
precisely the content of \cite[Theorem~3.1]{gaiotto-rapchak}.
Hence the output is freely strongly generated, hence Koszul by
Corollary~\ref{cor:universal-koszul}.

\emph{Proof~3 \textup{(}Truncation of
$\mathcal{W}_{1+\infty}$\textup{)}.}
$Y_{N_1,N_2,N_3}[\Psi]$ is the quotient of
$\mathcal{W}_{1+\infty}[\Psi]$ by the ideal whose truncation
curve is $\sum_i N_i/\lambda_i = 1$ \cite[eq.~3.35]{gaiotto-rapchak}.
Since $\mathcal{W}_{1+\infty}[\Psi]$ is freely generated
(one generator at each integer spin) and the truncation kills
generators above a threshold while introducing no relations
among the survivors at generic~$\Psi$, the quotient inherits
free strong generation. Apply
Corollary~\ref{cor:universal-koszul}.

\emph{Proof~4 \textup{(}PBW spectral sequence\textup{)}.}
The generators of $Y_{N_1,N_2,N_3}[\Psi]$ at generic~$\Psi$
have conformal weights $1, 2, \ldots, s_{\max}$ (distinct
integers). Hence the $E_1$~page of the PBW spectral sequence
is $\barB(\operatorname{Sym}^{\mathrm{ch}}(V))$ with $V$ a
direct sum of lines of distinct conformal weight. By Priddy's
theorem, $\operatorname{Sym}^{\mathrm{ch}}(V)$ is classically
Koszul, forcing $E_2$-collapse: the bar cohomology is concentrated
in bar degree~$1$. This is chiral Koszulness by definition.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[The non-generic locus]
\label{rem:y-algebra-non-generic-locus}
\index{Y-algebra@$Y$-algebra!non-generic locus}
For $Y_{0,0,N}$, the truncation singularity
$\Psi_{\mathrm{sing}} = 1$ coincides with the degenerate
locus, so it introduces no additional obstruction. For
$Y_{N_1,N_2,N_3}$ with $N_2 \neq N_3$, the singularity
$\Psi_{\mathrm{sing}} = (N_3 - N_1)/(N_3 - N_2)$ is
genuinely new (e.g.\ $\Psi_{\mathrm{sing}} = 2$ for
$Y_{1,2,3}$). The admissible levels form a countable
subset of~$\bQ$ determined by the Kac--Kazhdan theorem
for the parent superalgebra. At these values, null
vectors may enter the bar-relevant range and Koszulness
becomes conditional on the Kac--Shapovalov criterion
(Theorem~\ref{thm:kac-shapovalov-koszulness}).
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Duality compatibility]
\label{rem:y-algebra-koszul-duality-compat}
\index{Y-algebra@$Y$-algebra!duality}
The Koszulness status is preserved by all three dualities
acting on $Y$-algebras:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)},nosep]
\item \emph{$S_3$ triality}: permutes the $N$-triple and acts
 on~$\Psi$ by M\"obius transformations. Since the Koszulness
 status depends only on the sorted triple, triality preserves it.
\item \emph{Feigin--Frenkel duality}:
 $\Psi \mapsto -\Psi$, preserving the $N$-triple.
\item \emph{Koszul duality} \textup{(}predicted\textup{)}:
 $\Psi \mapsto -\Psi$ with $N$-triple preserved.
 If $Y_{N_1,N_2,N_3}[\Psi]$ is Koszul, so is
 $Y_{N_1,N_2,N_3}[-\Psi]$, consistent with the prediction that
 the Koszul dual is the FF-dual.
\end{enumerate}
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Shadow depth classification]
\label{rem:y-algebra-depth-classification}
\index{Y-algebra@$Y$-algebra!shadow depth}
\index{shadow depth!Y-algebra@$Y$-algebra}
Koszulness holds uniformly across all shadow depth classes.
The $Y$-algebra landscape exhibits two of the four classes:
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{llll}
\toprule
Class & $r_{\max}$ & Representative & Structure \\
\midrule
G & $2$ & $Y_{0,0,0}$, $Y_{0,0,1}$, $Y_{1,1,1}$ & free/Gaussian \\
M & $\infty$ & $Y_{0,0,N}$ ($N \geq 2$), $Y_{1,1,2}$, \ldots & W-type \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
Class~L (Lie/tree, $r_{\max} = 3$) and class~C (contact,
$r_{\max} = 4$) do not appear at generic coupling.
$Y_{1,1,1}[\Psi]$ is class~G despite $c = 0$
(Chapter~\ref{chap:y-algebras}): its generators are a
Heisenberg current and a $c = 0$ stress tensor, both
Gaussian. This confirms that shadow depth classifies complexity
\emph{within} the Koszul world, not Koszulness itself.
(The operator-order trichotomy (Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-depth-operator-order}) refines the $\mathsf{G}/\mathsf{L}/\mathsf{C}/\mathsf{M}$ classification at genus~$0$.)
\end{remark}


%% ================================================================
\section{The $N\!=\!2$ superconformal shadow obstruction tower}%
\label{sec:n2-shadow-tower}
\index{N=2 superconformal algebra@$N=2$ superconformal algebra!shadow tower}
\index{shadow obstruction tower!N=2 superconformal@$N=2$ superconformal}
\index{Kazama--Suzuki coset!shadow data}

The $N = 2$ superconformal algebra (SCA) is the extended chiral algebra
generated by the stress tensor~$T$, a $U(1)$ current~$J$, and a pair
of fermionic supercurrents $G^\pm$ of conformal weight~$3/2$. Its
central charge is $c = 3k/(k+2)$ where $k$ is the level of the
underlying $\mathfrak{sl}_2$ in the Kazama--Suzuki coset construction.
The shadow obstruction tower data of the $N=2$ SCA provides the first worked
example of a \emph{multi-channel} shadow obstruction tower with a $2 \times 2$
bosonic shadow metric.

\subsection{The modular characteristic: three routes}%
\label{subsec:n2-kappa-three-routes}

\begin{theorem}[$N=2$ modular characteristic; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{thm:n2-kappa}
\index{kappa@$\kappa$!N=2 superconformal@$N=2$ superconformal}
\index{N=2 superconformal algebra@$N=2$ superconformal algebra!kappa}
The modular characteristic of the $N = 2$ SCA at central charge
$c = 3k/(k+2)$ is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:n2-kappa}
\kappa(N{=}2) \;=\; \frac{k+4}{4} \;=\; \frac{6-c}{2(3-c)}.
\end{equation}
This is established by three independent routes:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \emph{Kazama--Suzuki coset decomposition:}
$\kappa(N{=}2) = \kappa(\mathfrak{sl}_{2,k}) + \kappa(\text{fermion})
- \kappa(U(1)) = \tfrac{3(k+2)}{4} + \tfrac{1}{2}
- (\tfrac{k}{2}+1) = \tfrac{k+4}{4}$.
\item \emph{DS reduction of $\mathfrak{sl}(2|1)$:}
The Kazama--Suzuki coset is isomorphic to the DS reduction
of $\mathfrak{sl}(2|1)_k$; the $\kappa$ computation via the
superalgebra realization gives the same result.
\item \emph{Spectral flow consistency:}
The spectral flow automorphism $\sigma_\theta$ preserves all
structure constants and hence all shadow coefficients.
Any valid $\kappa$ formula must be spectral-flow invariant.
Both~\eqref{eq:n2-kappa} and the incorrect formula $\kappa = 7c/6$
pass this test \textup{(}both depend only on $k$, not on
$\theta$\textup{)}; the distinction comes from route~\textup{(i)}.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Route~(i) is the coset decomposition. The Kazama--Suzuki
construction realizes the $N=2$ SCA as the commutant of $U(1)$
inside $\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_{2,k} \otimes (\text{complex fermion})$.
By additivity of $\kappa$ under tensor products and subtractivity
under cosets (Theorem~D):
\[
\kappa(N{=}2) = \kappa(\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_{2,k})
+ \kappa(\psi\bar\psi) - \kappa(\widehat{U(1)}).
\]
Computing each term:
$\kappa(\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_{2,k}) = 3(k+2)/4$
(dimension $3$, $h^\vee = 2$),
$\kappa(\psi\bar\psi) = 1/2$ (complex free fermion),
$\kappa(\widehat{U(1)}) = k/2 + 1$ (Heisenberg at the
appropriate level). Summing:
$3(k+2)/4 + 1/2 - k/2 - 1 = 3k/4 + 3/2 + 1/2 - k/2 - 1
= k/4 + 1 = (k+4)/4$.

To express in terms of $c$: from $c = 3k/(k+2)$,
$k = 2c/(3-c)$, so $(k+4)/4 = (2c/(3-c) + 4)/4
= (2c + 12 - 4c)/(4(3-c)) = (12-2c)/(4(3-c)) = (6-c)/(2(3-c))$.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Koszul duality and complementarity}%
\label{subsec:n2-koszul-duality}

\begin{proposition}[$N=2$ Koszul duality; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{prop:n2-koszul-duality}
\index{Koszul duality!N=2 superconformal@$N=2$ superconformal}
\index{N=2 superconformal algebra@$N=2$ superconformal algebra!Koszul duality}
The $N = 2$ Koszul duality acts as the \emph{additive} involution
$c \mapsto 6 - c$ \textup{(}equivalently, $k \mapsto -k-4$\textup{)}.
The complementarity sum is constant:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:n2-complementarity}
\kappa(c) + \kappa(6-c) \;=\; 1.
\end{equation}
The self-dual point is $c = 3$ \textup{(}$k \to \infty$, the free-field
limit\textup{)}, where $\kappa$ has a simple pole.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
$\kappa(c) + \kappa(6-c) = (6-c)/(2(3-c)) + c/(2(c-3))
= (6-c)/(2(3-c)) - c/(2(3-c)) = (6-2c)/(2(3-c)) = 1$.
The Feigin--Frenkel involution for $\mathfrak{sl}_2$ is
$k \mapsto -k - 2h^\vee = -k - 4$. Under this:
$c(-k-4) = 3(-k-4)/(-k-2) = 3(k+4)/(k+2) = 6 - c(k)$.
At $c = 3$: $\kappa(3) = (6-3)/(2 \cdot 0)$, which diverges;
$c = 3$ is the free-field limit, unreachable at finite~$k$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Chiral Koszulness of the $N=2$ SCA]%
\label{rem:n2-sca-koszulness}%
\index{N=2 superconformal algebra@$N=2$ superconformal algebra!Koszulness}%
\index{Koszul property!N=2 superconformal@$N=2$ superconformal}%
\index{Chevalley--Eilenberg complex!upper bound on bar cohomology}%
The $N = 2$ SCA is chirally Koszul at all central charges.
The algebra is freely strongly generated by $T$, $J$, $G^+$, $G^-$
\textup{(}Adamovi\'c~\cite{Adamovic1999}\textup{)}, so
PBW universality \textup{(}Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:pbw-universality}}\textup{)}
applies.

This requires a remark on an apparent paradox. The
Chevalley--Eilenberg complex of the mode algebra $\fg_-$
\textup{(}the truncation of the bar complex to mode-$0$ brackets\textup{)}
has $H^2_{\mathrm{CE}} \neq 0$ starting at half-weight~$5$;
at conformal weight~$3$ \textup{(}half-weight~$6$\textup{)},
$\dim H^2_{\mathrm{CE}} = 5$. The fermionic pair
$(G^+_{-3/2}, G^-_{-3/2})$ contributes a CE~$2$-cocycle that
the sub-leading OPE mode $d_1$ does \emph{not} remove, because
$d_1(G^+ \wedge G^-) = G^+_{(1)}G^- + G^-_{(1)}G^+
= J + (-J) = 0$
\textup{(}supersymmetric cancellation\textup{)}.

The resolution is that the CE complex is a \emph{coarse upper bound}
on the chiral bar cohomology: it retains only the mode-$0$
bracket, discarding the full OPE pole structure and the
geometric corrections from configuration spaces
$\Conf_n(X)$. The chiral bar differential uses the complete
OPE \textup{(}all poles of $a(z)b(w)$\textup{)}, and the
geometric structure of $\Conf_n(X)$ provides additional
coboundaries that kill the CE cocycles. In particular,
PBW universality proves $H^2(\barB(\cA)) = 0$ for any
freely strongly generated $\cA$, regardless of the CE cohomology.

This illustrates a general principle: the CE complex
$\Lambda^*(\fg_-)$ surjects onto the $E_1$ page of the
bar spectral sequence but need not inject into the bar
cohomology. Non-vanishing $H^2_{\mathrm{CE}}$ is necessary
for non-Koszulness \textup{(}if $H^2_{\mathrm{CE}} = 0$, the
algebra is automatically Koszul\textup{)} but \emph{not
sufficient}: the chiral bar differential is strictly finer than
the CE differential.
\end{remark}

\subsection{Channel-refined shadow metric}%
\label{subsec:n2-channel-shadow-metric}

\begin{proposition}[$N=2$ channel decomposition; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{prop:n2-channel-decomposition}
\index{N=2 superconformal algebra@$N=2$ superconformal algebra!channel decomposition}
\index{shadow metric!N=2 channels@$N=2$ channels}
The bosonic sector of the $N = 2$ SCA decomposes into two primary
lines with distinct shadow data:
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{lccccc}
\toprule
Channel & $\kappa$ & $\alpha$ & $S_4$ & $\Delta$ & Class \\
\midrule
$T$-line \textup{(Virasoro)} & $c/2$ & $2$ & $10/[c(5c+22)]$ &
 $40/(5c+22)$ & M \\
$J$-line \textup{(Heisenberg)} & $c/3$ & $0$ & $0$ & $0$ & G \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The $T$-line inherits the full Virasoro shadow structure
\textup{(}class~M, infinite shadow depth\textup{)}. The $J$-line is
a free Heisenberg channel \textup{(}class~G, shadow depth~$2$\textup{)}: the
$U(1)$ current $J$ has no nonlinear self-OPE, so $\alpha_J = 0$ and
$S_4^J = 0$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The $T$-channel data is the Virasoro shadow at central charge~$c$
(the $N=2$ stress tensor is the Sugawara tensor of the full algebra).
The $J$-channel: $J_{(1)}J = c/3$ (the $U(1)$ level), giving
$\kappa_J = c/3$, and $J_{(0)}J = 0$ (abelian), so $\alpha_J = 0$
and the tower terminates at degree~$2$.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[$N=2$ bosonic shadow metric; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{prop:n2-bosonic-shadow-metric}
\index{shadow metric!N=2 bosonic@$N=2$ bosonic}
The $2 \times 2$ shadow metric in the $(T, J)$ bosonic basis is:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:n2-shadow-metric-matrix}
Q^{(2)} \;=\; \begin{pmatrix}
(c + 6t)^2 + \tfrac{80}{5c+22}\, t^2 & 0 \\
0 & 4c^2/9
\end{pmatrix}
\end{equation}
at degree~$2$. The off-diagonal $T$-$J$ coupling enters at
degree~$3$ through the structure constant $T_{(1)}J = J$. The
$J$-channel entry is constant \textup{(}no $t$-dependence\textup{)}:
$Q_J = (2\kappa_J)^2 = 4c^2/9$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The diagonal entries are $Q_T(t) = (2\kappa_T + 3\alpha_T t)^2
+ 2\Delta_T t^2 = (c + 6t)^2 + (80/(5c+22))t^2$ and
$Q_J = (2\kappa_J)^2 = (2c/3)^2 = 4c^2/9$. At degree~$2$ the
metric is diagonal; the off-diagonal $T$-$J$ mixing arises from
the cubic graph with one $T$ and one $J$ leg, which first
contributes at degree~$3$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Spectral flow invariance of the shadow obstruction tower]%
\label{rem:n2-spectral-flow-invariance}
\index{spectral flow!shadow invariance}
\index{N=2 superconformal algebra@$N=2$ superconformal algebra!spectral flow}
The spectral flow $\sigma_\theta$ of the $N = 2$ algebra is an
automorphism that maps the NS sector to the Ramond sector
(at $\theta = 1/2$). Since automorphisms preserve all OPE
structure constants, they preserve every shadow coefficient:
$S_r(\mathrm{NS}) = S_r(\mathrm{R})$ for all $r$. In
particular, $\kappa$, $S_3$, $S_4$, and $\rho$ are identical
in both sectors. This is a non-trivial consistency check on
the shadow obstruction tower framework: the NS and R sectors have different
field content (integer vs.\ half-integer moded supercurrents),
but the shadow data, being determined by the OPE algebra, is
spectral-flow invariant.
\end{remark}

\subsection{$N=2$ minimal models}%
\label{subsec:n2-minimal-models}

\begin{proposition}[$N=2$ minimal model shadow data; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{prop:n2-minimal-models}
\index{N=2 superconformal algebra@$N=2$ superconformal algebra!minimal models}
\index{minimal model!N=2@$N=2$!shadow data}
The $N = 2$ unitary minimal models at $c = 3k/(k+2)$ for
$k = 1, 2, 3, 4$ have the following shadow data:
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{cccccc}
\toprule
$k$ & $c$ & $\kappa$ & $c' = 6-c$ & $\kappa'$ & $\kappa + \kappa'$ \\
\midrule
$1$ & $1$ & $5/4$ & $5$ & $-1/4$ & $1$ \\
$2$ & $3/2$ & $3/2$ & $9/2$ & $-1/2$ & $1$ \\
$3$ & $9/5$ & $7/4$ & $21/5$ & $-3/4$ & $1$ \\
$4$ & $2$ & $2$ & $4$ & $-1$ & $1$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
Every entry satisfies $\kappa + \kappa' = 1$
\textup{(}Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:n2-koszul-duality})}.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Direct evaluation of $\kappa = (k+4)/4$ and $\kappa' = (-k)/4$
at each value of~$k$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[The Gepner model and the quintic threefold]%
\label{rem:gepner-model}
\index{Gepner model}
\index{Calabi--Yau!quintic threefold}
Five copies of the $k = 3$ minimal model (each at $c = 9/5$) form
the Gepner model $(3,3,3,3,3)$, the exactly solvable sigma model
on the Fermat quintic threefold in $\mathbb{CP}^4$. By additivity:
$c_{\mathrm{total}} = 5 \cdot 9/5 = 9$ and
$\kappa_{\mathrm{total}} = 5 \cdot 7/4 = 35/4$. The shadow obstruction tower
of the Gepner model is the direct sum of five independent copies,
each class~M on the $T$-channel and class~G on the $J$-channel.
The total $T$-line shadow growth rate is that of the Virasoro at
$c = 9$, while the Heisenberg channels remain Gaussian.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Elliptic genus and Mathieu moonshine]%
\label{rem:n2-elliptic-genus}
\index{elliptic genus!K3}
\index{Mathieu moonshine}
At $c = 6$ (the K3 sigma model, with $N = (4,4)$ supersymmetry),
the elliptic genus is $Z_{\mathrm{ell}}(\tau, z) = 2\phi_{0,1}(\tau, z)$,
where $\phi_{0,1}$ is the unique weak Jacobi form of weight~$0$
and index~$1$. Setting $z = 0$:
$Z_{\mathrm{ell}}(\tau, 0) = 24 = \chi(\mathrm{K3})$.
The Fourier expansion
$2\phi_{0,1} = 2(y + 10 + y^{-1}) + (20y^2 + 216y + \cdots)q + \cdots$
exhibits Mathieu moonshine (Eguchi--Ooguri--Tachikawa 2010):
the coefficients of the mock modular form
$H(\tau) = \sum_{n \ge 0} A_n q^{n - 1/8}$ decompose into
dimensions of irreducible $M_{24}$ representations:
$A_1 = 90 = 45 + 45'$, $A_2 = 462 = 231 + 231'$.
The shadow obstruction tower of the $c = 6$ algebra, via the Kazama--Suzuki
construction at $k = -4 + \varepsilon$, packages the elliptic genus
as the genus-$1$ shadow partition function in the Ramond sector.
\end{remark}

\subsection{The Pixton ideal from the shadow obstruction tower}%
\label{subsec:pixton-from-shadows}

Pixton's conjecture (Pixton, \emph{Conjectural relations on
$\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n}$}, arXiv:1207.1918, 2012) posits that
the tautological relations on $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n}$ are
generated by an explicit polynomial in the $\psi$- and $\kappa$-classes
(the \emph{Pixton polynomial}), building on the double-ramification
cycle formula of Janda--Pandharipande--Pixton--Zvonkine~\cite{JPPZ18}
and the $3$-spin relations of Pandharipande--Pixton--Zvonkine~\cite{PPZ19}.
Write $I_{\mathrm{Pix}}(g,n)
\subset R^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n})$ for the ideal generated
by these relations; we call it the \emph{Pixton ideal}. The following
conjecture relates $I_{\mathrm{Pix}}$ to the shadow obstruction tower
of class-M chiral algebras.

\begin{conjecture}[Pixton ideal from shadow tower; ;
\ClaimStatusConjectured]%
\label{conj:pixton-from-shadows}
\index{Pixton ideal!from shadow tower}
\index{tautological ring!Pixton relations}
\index{shadow obstruction tower!Pixton ideal}
Let $\cA$ be a class-M chiral algebra
(Virasoro, $\mathcal{W}_N$ for $N \geq 2$, or $\mathcal{W}_\infty$)
with infinite shadow obstruction tower
$\{\mathrm{Sh}_r(\cA)\}_{r \geq 2}$
\textup{(}Definition of $\mathrm{Sh}_r(\cA) = \Theta_{\cA}^{\leq r}$ as
in the degree filtration of the all-degree MC element
$\Theta_{\cA}$: Theorem~\ref{thm:mc2-bar-intrinsic}
and Theorem~\ref{thm:recursive-existence}\textup{)}.
Assume the \emph{flat identity hypothesis}: the vacuum
$|0\rangle \in \cA$ lies in the generating space used to
propagate the MC element to the Feynman transform of the modular
operad governing $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n}$.
Then the degree-indexed projection of the MC equation
\begin{equation}\label{eq:pixton-MC}
D \cdot \Theta_{\cA} + \tfrac{1}{2}[\Theta_{\cA},\Theta_{\cA}] = 0,
\qquad
\Theta_{\cA} = \sum_{r \geq 2} \frac{1}{r!}\,\Theta_{\cA}^{(r)},
\end{equation}
pushed forward through the Feynman transform to
$\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n}$ under the uniform-weight
CohFT transport, \emph{implies} the Pixton polynomial relations:
the image of the tower
$\{\mathrm{Sh}_r(\cA)\}_{r \geq 2}$ in
$R^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n})$ generates
$I_{\mathrm{Pix}}(g,n)$ for every stable $(g,n)$ with
$2g-2+n > 0$.
\end{conjecture}

\begin{remark}[Genus-$2$ and genus-$3$ Virasoro verification]%
\label{rem:pixton-genus2-verification}
\index{Pixton ideal!genus-2 verification}
For $\cA = \mathrm{Vir}_c$, the genus-$2$ and genus-$3$ projections
of~\eqref{eq:pixton-MC} have been computed directly from the
shadow data $(\kappa, \alpha, S_4, \rho)$ of the Virasoro algebra
and matched against Pixton's polynomial formula at these genera
\textup{(}compute engines
\texttt{test\_pixton\_genus3\_shadow\_engine.py} and
\texttt{test\_pixton\_shadow\_bridge.py}\textup{)}. Agreement
holds to the full order of the tabulated relations. The
computations use OPE modes (Vol~I convention) and the
uniform-weight CohFT identification; no multi-weight
cross-channel correction enters at these genera because the
Virasoro stress tensor is the unique weight-$2$ generator.
The Givental--Gromov quantization of the KdV hierarchy provides
an independent cross-check at genus~$2$ via the
Buryak--Shadrin--Spitz--Zvonkine identification of the Pixton
relations with integrable-system tau-function constraints.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Class-M specificity]%
\label{rem:pixton-class-m-only}
\index{Pixton ideal!class-M specificity}
Conjecture~\ref{conj:pixton-from-shadows} is \emph{specific to
class~M}. For class~G (Heisenberg, rank $r = 2$), class~L (affine
Kac--Moody at nonzero level, rank $r = 3$), and class~C
($\beta\gamma$ and similar, rank $r = 4$), the shadow obstruction
tower terminates at finite degree and the projected MC element
$\Theta_{\cA}$ is a polynomial of bounded degree in the tautological
generators. The corresponding image in
$R^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n})$ lies in the subring generated
by a finite set of $\psi$- and $\kappa$-polynomials, and the
Pixton ideal $I_{\mathrm{Pix}}(g,n)$ is trivial on the image.
The conjecture therefore has no content outside class~M; the
infinite shadow depth of Virasoro, $\mathcal{W}_N$, and
$\mathcal{W}_\infty$ is precisely what is required for the
MC tower to produce nontrivial tautological relations.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Scope and converse]%
\textup{(}LOCAL: scope\textup{})
\label{rem:pixton-scope-converse}
\index{Pixton ideal!scope}
Conjecture~\ref{conj:pixton-from-shadows} asserts only an
\emph{implication}: the shadow tower generates $I_{\mathrm{Pix}}$.
The converse, that every Pixton relation arises from a unique
shadow coefficient, is not claimed here and would require an
independent dimension count on both sides of the Feynman
transform. The flat identity hypothesis is essential:
without a vacuum in the generating space the degree-$r$ projection
does not descend to $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n}$ as a flat
CohFT class, and the MC tower transports only to a non-unital
Feynman transform. At $g \geq 2$ in the multi-weight setting,
a cross-channel correction $\delta F_g^{\mathrm{cross}}$ modifies
the scalar projection and the scalar-only reading fails; the
uniform-weight
tag above restricts the conjecture to the regime where this
correction vanishes.
\end{remark}

\section{Synthesis}
\label{sec:walgdeep-supplement}

\begin{remark}[Class-$\mathcal S$ $A_1$ on $\Sigma_{0,24}$: the $W$-algebraic face]
\label{rem:walgdeep-1}
The deep $W$-algebra theory assembled here meets the K3 structure at a
single class-$\mathcal S$ theory. On a $24$-punctured sphere
$\Sigma_{0,24}$ of genus zero, the Gaiotto $2009$ class-$\mathcal S$
construction with Lie-algebra label $A_1$ produces a $4$d $\mathcal N=2$
superconformal theory with canonical invariants
(Shapere--Tachikawa $2008$; Chacaltana--Distler $2010$;
Beem--Lemos--Liendo--Peelaers--Rastelli--van~Rees $2013$):
\[
c_{4d} \;=\; \tfrac{5\cdot 24 - 13}{6} \;=\; \tfrac{107}{6},
\qquad
c_{2d} \;=\; -12\,c_{4d} \;=\; -214,
\qquad
\mathrm{rank}(\mathrm{Coulomb}) = 21,
\qquad
\mathrm{flavour} = \mathfrak{su}(2)^{24}.
\]
The $2$d chiral algebra $\chi[\mathcal T(A_1,\Sigma_{0,24})]$ via the
BLLPRvR 2013 SCFT-to-VOA functor is a non-abelian chiral $W$-algebra of
central charge $c_{2d} = -214$, whose representation theory matches
$\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ through the Frenkel--Kac 1980 vertex-operator
closure on the K3 Fock space $\mathcal F_{K3}$. See Vol.~III
Remark~\ref{V3-rem:k3-classS-numerical-caveat} and
Proposition~\ref{V3-prop:k3-chacaltana-distler-24} for the double-retraction
record of the intermediate evaluation $(c_{4d}, c_{2d})
= (26, -312)$ which failed the $\mathrm{SU}(2)$ $N_f = 4$ cross-check.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Andrianov $L$-function: $L(s,\Delta_{10}) = L(s,\Delta\otimes E_6)\,\zeta(s-9)\zeta(s-8)$]
\label{rem:walgdeep-2}
The deep $W$-algebra $W_N$ families tabulated here admit an arithmetic
shadow through the Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998 Igusa cusp form $\Phi_{10}$
on $\bar{\mathcal A}_2$. The Andrianov spinor $L$-function factorisation
\[
L(s,\Phi_{10}) \;=\; L(s,\Delta\otimes E_6)\cdot \zeta(s-9)\cdot \zeta(s-8),
\]
where $\Delta$ is the Ramanujan weight-$12$ cusp form and $E_6$ the
weight-$6$ Eisenstein series, decomposes the $W$-algebraic Hecke spectrum
on $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ into three pieces: a Ramanujan-type arithmetic
factor $L(s,\Delta\otimes E_6)$, and two degree-$1$ $\zeta$-shifts
encoding the Mukai $c_\pm$ signature-$(4,20)$ pairing. The $(s-9,s-8)$
shifts are not accidents: $9 = c_-/2 - 1$, $8 = K^{\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}}$,
matching the Bruinier 2002 Chern-class reciprocity on $H_1$.
Primary-lit: Andrianov 1974, Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998, Arthur 2004.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Frenkel--Kac closure on the K3 Fock space]
\label{rem:walgdeep-3}
The Frenkel--Kac 1980 construction, originally stated for simply-laced
affine Kac--Moody level-$1$ modules, extends to the Mukai lattice
$\Lambda_{\mathrm{Muk}} = II_{4,20}$ through the choice of $24$
distinguished lattice vectors matching the $24$ Kodaira I$_1$ fibres
of $E^{\mathrm{nod,sm}}_{24}$. The resulting vertex-operator closure on
the K3 Fock space $\mathcal F_{K3} = \mathrm{Sym}^\bullet(\Lambda_{\mathrm{Muk}}\otimes\mathbb C[t,t^{-1}])$
is exactly $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}\!\mid_{\hbar\to 0}$. The deep-$W$ generators
$W_k$, $k\ge 3$, lift to higher-spin vertex operators on $\mathcal F_{K3}$
carrying $M_{24}$-equivariance via the Steiner system $S(5,8,24)$, which
recovers the Eguchi--Ooguri--Tachikawa 2011 moonshine observation at
the classical limit. At $\hbar^2 = -1/8$ the $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ quantisation
deforms this closure through the Siegel-elliptic dynamical $R$-matrix
$R_{\mathrm{Sieg,dyn}}$ and the $\widetilde{M}_{24}$ Schur cocycle of
order~$6$.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Class-$\mathcal S$ $A_{N-1}$ $N$-parametric table]
\label{rem:walgdeep-W16-gaiotto-N-table}
The $N=2$ retraction is naturally extended to the
whole $A_{N-1}$ family on the $24$-punctured sphere. Applying the
Gaiotto 2009 pants decomposition with $3g-3+n = 21$ $\mathfrak{su}(N)$
gauge tubes and $2g-2+n = 22$ trinions $T_N$, and importing the
Chacaltana--Distler 2010 (arXiv:1008.5203) Tab.\ 3 trinion anomaly data
\[
n_v(T_N) = \tfrac{(N-1)(N-2)(N+2)}{2},\qquad
n_h(T_N) = \tfrac{2N(N^2-1)}{3},
\]
fitted across $N\in\{2,3,4,5\}$, one computes
\[
n_v = 21(N^2-1) + 22\cdot n_v(T_N),\qquad
n_h = 22\cdot n_h(T_N),
\]
and $(a_{4d},c_{4d}) = ((5n_v+n_h)/24,\,(2n_v+n_h)/12)$. The results are:

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{c|ccccc}
$N$ & $n_v$ & $n_h$ & $c_{4d}$ & $c_{2d} = -12\,c_{4d}$ & $\dim_\mathbb{C}\mathrm{Coulomb}$ \\\hline
$2$ & $63$ & $88$ & $107/6$ & $-214$ & $21$ \\
$3$ & $278$ & $352$ & $227/3$ & $-908$ & $42$ \\
$4$ & $711$ & $880$ & $1151/6$ & $-2302$ & $63$ \\
$5$ & $1428$ & $1760$ & $1154/3$ & $-4616$ & $84$ \\
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

The $N=2$ row recovers the corrected values; it passes the
$\mathrm{SU}(2)$ $N_f=4$ SQCD cross-check
($c_{4d}(A_1,\Sigma_{0,4}) = 7/6$, Shapere--Tachikawa 2008) under
the same formula. The $N=3$ row passes the E$_6$ Minahan--Nemeschansky
cross-check ($T_3 = \mathcal T[A_2,\Sigma_{0,3}]$ has $n_v = 5$,
$n_h = 16$, $c_{4d} = 26/3$; Minahan--Nemeschansky 1996; Argyres--Seiberg 2007).
Flavour subalgebras are $\widehat{\mathfrak{su}(N)}_{k_{2d}}^{\otimes 24}$
with $k_{2d} = -N$ per puncture (Beem--Rastelli 2015, eq.\ (3.7)).
Primary-lit: Gaiotto 2009 (arXiv:0904.2715); Chacaltana--Distler 2010
(arXiv:1008.5203); Shapere--Tachikawa 2008 (arXiv:0804.1957);
Tachikawa 2013 notes (arXiv:1312.2684) Ch.~13;
Beem--Lemos--Liendo--Peelaers--Rastelli--van~Rees 2015 (arXiv:1312.5344);
Beem--Rastelli 2015 (arXiv:1404.1079); Minahan--Nemeschansky 1996
