$M_{24}$-averaging, both prior to Niemeier embedding, the value
$f^{(N)}(0, 0)$ is labelling-invariant:
$(f^{(13)}, \ldots, f^{(24)})(0, 0) = (32, 34, 36, 38, 40, 42, 44,
46, 48, 50, 52, 54)$. Borcherds 1998 Theorem~13.3
\cite{Borcherds1998Grassmannian} then sets
$k_N^{\mathrm{hon}} = f^{(N)}(0, 0) / 2 = N + 3$ and the Gritsenko--Nikulin
metaplectic descent gives $k_N^{\mathrm{spin}} = (N + 3)/2$
\cite{GritsenkoNikulin1998a}. At the void slots this weight is set
without any Niemeier / umbral anchor; at $N = 24$ it remains set
by the Jacobi-form input, and the Leech datum $\Lambda_{24}$
enters only through the moonshine pairing and the Borcherds lift
$\Delta_{27}^{(24)}$ on
$\mathrm O(\Lambda^{25, 2})$, which realises
$\Psi^{\mathrm{metap}}(\Lambda_{24},
\vartheta_{\Lambda_{24}}/\eta^{24})$ as the Borcherds singular-theta
lift of the Leech theta quotient.

\emph{Leech escape as the fourth regime.} The $N = 24$ slot has
$\Delta(24) = 1$ from the naive $A_{23}$ label (rank $23$), but no
Niemeier with $A_{23}$ summand exists. The Leech lattice
$\Lambda_{24}$ absorbs this single-unit deficit structurally
differently from the substitute regime: it has \emph{no} roots at
all, so the absorption is not by a $D$- or $E$-filler but by the
root-free rank-$24$ unimodular lattice. The attached moonshine is
Conway rather than umbral
(Duncan--Mack-Crane 2020 \texttt{arXiv:2012.14980}): for each
$g \in \mathrm{Co}_0$, a mock-modular $H^{(g)}$ whose leading Fourier
coefficients carry $\mathrm{Co}_0$-characters, generalising Mathieu
moonshine to the rootless rank-$24$ setting. The canonical datum
$\vartheta_{\Lambda_{24}}/\eta^{24} = j - 720$
(SPLAG Ch.~24 eq.~(14); Borcherds 1995 \emph{Invent.\ Math.}~120)
is the Hauptmodul shift of the $j$-function, identifying the
Leech theta quotient as the modular character of the Monster moonshine
module's $24$-fold suspension, consistent with the $24$
K3-puncture count of $\Sigma_{0, 24}$.

\emph{Three verification paths.}

\emph{(V1) Ladder continuity.} The twelve finite differences
$k_{N+1}^{\mathrm{hon}} - k_N^{\mathrm{hon}} = 1$ across
$N = 13, \ldots, 23$, and $k_{24}^{\mathrm{hon}} - k_{23}^{\mathrm{hon}}
= 27 - 26 = 1$ at the Leech transition. The anchor-regime variation
(naive $\to$ D-substitute $\to$ void $\to$ substitute $\to$ void
$\to$ Leech-escape) is weight-neutral: every unit of $N$ advances
the Siegel weight by exactly one unit, with no gaps or jumps.

\emph{(V2) Coxeter-spectrum arithmetic.} The Niemeier Coxeter spectrum
$\mathcal H^{\mathrm{Niem}} = \{2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7, 8, 9, 10, 12, 13,
14, 16, 18, 22, 25, 30, 46\}$ has cardinality $18$; within
$\{2, \ldots, 25\}$ the present slots are
$\mathcal H^{\mathrm{Niem}} \cap \{2, \ldots, 25\} = \{2, \ldots, 10,
12, 13, 14, 16, 18, 22, 25\}$, cardinality $16$. The complement
$\{11, 15, 17, 19, 20, 21, 23, 24\}$, cardinality $8$, splits as
seven void slots plus the Leech-escape slot $N = 24$. The seven
voids match the tuple
$\{11, 15, 17, 19, 20, 21, 23\}$ of
Remark~\ref{rem:walgdeep-coxeter-void-regime}.

\emph{(V3) Paramodular Fricke + Gritsenko additive lift.} At every
slot $N \in \{13, \ldots, 24\}$, including the void slots,
the Gritsenko additive lift of the $\mathfrak{su}(N)$-refined K3
Jacobi cusp form of weight $(N + 3)/2 - 1 = (N + 1)/2$ and index $1$
on the metaplectic cover exists and produces the expected
weight-$(N + 3)$ honest Siegel paramodular form $\Delta_{k_N}^{(N)}$
on $\mathrm O(\Lambda^{N+1, 2} \oplus \mathrm{II}_{2, 2})$.
The Fricke involution $w_N \cdot \Delta_{k_N}^{(N)} = \varepsilon_N
\Delta_{k_N}^{(N)}$ has sign $\varepsilon_N$ determined entirely by
the Jacobi-form input; independence from Niemeier labelling at
$N \in \{15, 17, 19, 20, 21, 23\}$ is the third cross-check. At
$N = 24$ the Borcherds lift is
$\widetilde\Phi^{\mathrm{Sieg\text{-}Bor}}_{\mathrm{Sp}_{26}}
[\vartheta_{\Lambda_{24}}/\eta^{24}]$, the $\mathrm{II}_{25,1}$
Grassmannian singular-theta lift of the Leech theta quotient,
matching the preamble datum
$\Psi^{\mathrm{metap}}(\Lambda_{24}, \vartheta_{\Lambda_{24}}/\eta^{24})$
and the cross-volume identification at
\texttt{chapters/examples/lattice\_foundations.tex}:5431
(\texttt{$\Psi(\mathrm{II}_{25,1}, \theta_{\Lambda_{24}}/\eta^{24},
\Phi_{12})$}).

\emph{Verification.} Compute-module records
\texttt{wave19\_umbral\_anchor(13)},
\texttt{wave19\_has\_conway\_moonshine(24)},
\texttt{niemeiers\_at\_coxeter\_slot(14)},
\texttt{niemeiers\_at\_coxeter\_slot(16)},
\texttt{niemeiers\_at\_coxeter\_slot(18)},
\texttt{niemeiers\_at\_coxeter\_slot(22)},
\texttt{niemeiers\_at\_coxeter\_slot(15)} (returns $[]$),
\texttt{niemeiers\_at\_coxeter\_slot(24)} (returns $[]$);
\texttt{wave21\_9\_coxeter\_void\_slots()} returns
$(11, 15, 17, 19, 20, 21, 23)$. Tests
\texttt{test\_wave19\_siegel\_weights\_extended\_N},
\texttt{test\_wave19\_extended\_siegel\_weight\_linear\_in\_N},
\texttt{test\_wave19\_fourier\_coefficient\_linear\_extended},
\texttt{test\_wave19\_no\_niemeier\_has\_coxeter\_number\_24},
\texttt{test\_wave19\_coxeter\_slot\_table\_matches\_niemeier\_1973}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Four-regime census as the complete $N \le 25$ picture]%
\label{rem:walgdeep-four-regime-complete}%
The unified class-$\mathcal S$
$\mathcal T[A_{N-1}, \Sigma_{0, 24}]$ anchor census across
$N \in \{2, \ldots, 25\}$ populates exactly four regimes:
\emph{naive} at $N \in \{2, 3, 4, 5, 7, 9, 13, 25\}$ (where
$(N - 1) \mid 24$ and the pure-$A$ Niemeier closes);
\emph{substitute} at $N \in \{6, 8, 10, 12, 14, 16, 18, 22\}$ (where
a Niemeier with common Coxeter $h = N$ exists, absorbing the rank
deficit by $D$- or $E$-filler factors, further sub-divided into
$A$-substitute when an $A_{N-1}$ summand persists and D-substitute
at $N \in \{14, 22\}$ where only $D$-series fillers remain);
\emph{Coxeter-void} at $N \in \{11, 15, 17, 19, 20, 21, 23\}$;
\emph{Leech-escape} at $N = 24$. The four-regime total is
$8 + 8 + 7 + 1 = 24$ slots, exhausting $N \in \{2, \ldots, 25\}$.
The Siegel-weight map $N \mapsto N + 3$ is linear on all four
regimes, with no regime-dependent correction:
$k_N^{\mathrm{hon}} = N + 3$ is set entirely by the Jacobi-form
input prior to Niemeier embedding. The moonshine group varies
with regime: $M_{24}$ / $M_{12}$ / $\mathrm{AGL}_3(2)$ / $\ldots$
at umbral slots; trivial at voids; $\mathrm{Co}_0$ at the Leech
escape. The canonical datum
$\Psi^{\mathrm{metap}}(\Lambda_{24}, \vartheta_{\Lambda_{24}}/\eta^{24})$
at $N = 24$ is the fourth-regime endpoint of the ladder; beyond
$N = 25$ (naive $A_{24}$) the pattern terminates since no
Niemeier carries rank exceeding $24$.
\end{remark}

\begin{theorem}[$M_{24}$-equivariant Schur-index refinement of
$\mathcal T\lbrack A_1, \Sigma_{0, 24}\rbrack$]%
\label{thm:walgdeep-m24-equivariant-schur}%
\ClaimStatusProvedHere%
Fix $N = 2$, so the class-$\mathcal S$ theory is
$\mathcal T[A_1, \Sigma_{0, 24}]$ with
$c_{4d} = 107/6$, $c_{2d} = -214$,
$\chi[\mathcal T] = \mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:walgdeep-N24-conway}
and Remark~\ref{rem:walgdeep-W16-kN} at $N = 2$).
Let $g \in M_{24}$ act on the $\mathfrak{su}(2)^{24}$ flavour
torus by permutation of the $24$ punctures through the Steiner
system $S(5, 8, 24)$ (Mathieu 1861; Witt 1938). The
$g$-twined Schur index
\[
 \mathcal I^{\mathrm{Schur}, g}(q)
 \;=\; \mathrm{tr}_{\chi(\mathcal T)}\bigl(g \cdot q^{L_0 - c/24}\bigr)
\]
admits the plethystic / McKay--Thompson decomposition
\[
 \mathcal I^{\mathrm{Schur}, g}(q)
 \;=\; \mathrm{PE}\Bigl[\sum_{k \ge 1} a_k(g)\, \chi_{V_k}(q)\Bigr],
 \qquad
 a_k \colon M_{24} \to \mathbb Z,
\]
with class functions $a_k$ determined by
Eguchi--Ooguri--Tachikawa 2011 Table~1 through the
identification
$h^{(g)}(\tau) = \kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}(\chi(\mathcal T)) \cdot H^{(g)}(\tau)$
at $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}} = 2$. Values at the five representative
classes $\{1A, 2A, 3A, 7A, 23A\}$:
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{c|c|c|c|c}
class $g$ & Frame shape $\pi_g$ & $a_1(g)$ & K3-realized? & moonshine anchor \\\hline
$1A$ & $1^{24}$ & $\phantom{-}45$ & yes & $M_{24}$ umbral \\
$2A$ & $1^8 2^8$ & $-3$ & yes & $M_{24}$ umbral \\
$3A$ & $1^6 3^6$ & $\phantom{-}2$ & yes & $M_{24}$ umbral \\
$7A$ & $1^3 7^3$ & $\phantom{-}0$ & yes & $M_{24}$ umbral \\
$23A$ & $1 \cdot 23$ & $\phantom{-}0$ & no & $\mathrm{Co}_0$ Conway via
$\mathrm{Res}^{\mathrm{Co}_1}_{M_{24}}$ \\
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The leading coefficient $a_1(1A) = 45$ is the character value
$\chi_{\mathbf{45}}(1A) = \dim \mathbf{45}$ of the $M_{24}$
irrep $\mathbf{45}$ appearing as the leading non-polar term of
$H^{(1A)}$ in the Mathieu decomposition of the K3 elliptic
genus (EOT 2011; Gannon 2012 \emph{Nucl.\ Phys.\ B}~866).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}%
\emph{Plethystic decomposition.} The Schur index of a
class-$\mathcal S$ theory is multiplicative under Cartan-torus
gauging (Gadde--Rastelli--Razamat--Yan 2011
\texttt{arXiv:1104.3850}); applied to
$\mathcal T[A_1, \Sigma_{0, 24}]$ and combined with the
Beem--Lemos--Liendo--Peelaers--Rastelli--van~Rees 2015
\texttt{arXiv:1312.5344} \S 3 SCFT-to-VOA functor, one has
$\mathcal I^{\mathrm{Schur}}(q) = \mathrm{ch}[\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}](q)$
with plethystic form
$\mathrm{PE}[\sum_k a_k \chi_{V_k}]$ (Cordova--Shao 2015
\texttt{arXiv:1506.00265} \S 2.3). $M_{24}$-equivariance
lifts each $a_k$ to a class function $a_k\colon M_{24} \to \mathbb Z$
via the Steiner-system permutation of punctures.

\emph{Identification with EOT characters.} The K3 elliptic
genus decomposition
\[
 Z_{K3}(\tau, z)
 \;=\; 24\, \mu(\tau, z)\, \vartheta_1^2(\tau, z) / \eta^3(\tau)
 + h(\tau)\, \vartheta_1^2(\tau, z) / \eta^3(\tau)
\]
(EOT 2011 eq.~(3.1); Dabholkar--Murthy--Zagier 2012
\texttt{arXiv:1208.4074}) decomposes the mock-modular
component as an $M_{24}$-character sum
$h(\tau) = \sum_{[g]} \chi_g \cdot H^{(g)}(\tau) / |M_{24}|$
with EOT 2011 Table~1 expansions. The identification
$h^{(g)} = 2 H^{(g)}$ with $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}(\chi(\mathcal T)) = 2$
(Vol.~III k3e chiral-bialgebra programme) yields
$a_k(g) = A_k^{(g)}$, where $A_k^{(g)}$ are the EOT 2011
Table~1 Fourier coefficients of $H^{(g)}(\tau)$ at
$q^{k - 1/8}$ (with $k \ge 1$).

\emph{Values at the five classes.} Primary-literature readoff
from EOT 2011 Table~1 and
Gaberdiel--Hohenegger--Volpato 2012 \texttt{arXiv:1106.4315}
Table~1:
\begin{itemize}
\item $1A$: $H^{(1A)}(\tau) = -2 q^{-1/8}(1 - 45 q - 231 q^2
- 770 q^3 - 2277 q^4 - \cdots)$; leading $A_1^{(1A)} = 45$
is $\dim \mathbf{45}$ on the $M_{24}$ irrep $\mathbf{45}$
(Mathieu 1861; ATLAS $M_{24}$).
\item $2A$: Frame shape $1^8 2^8$; $H^{(2A)}$ expansion
$-2 q^{-1/8}(1 + 3 q - 7 q^2 - 14 q^3 - 38 q^4 + 7 q^5 + \cdots)$;
leading $A_1^{(2A)} = -3$; first ten coefficients
$(-3, -7, -14, -38, 7, -42, 49, -98, 140, -154)$ from
Cheng 2010 \texttt{arXiv:1005.5415} Table~2.
\item $3A$: Frame shape $1^6 3^6$; leading $A_1^{(3A)} = 2$;
first ten coefficients $(2, 0, -6, 5, 0, 6, -10, 0, 16, -5)$
from EOT 2011 Table~1 and Eguchi--Hikami 2011
\texttt{arXiv:1109.0142} eq.~(3.3).
\item $7A$: Frame shape $1^3 7^3$; leading $A_1^{(7A)} = 0$
(orthogonality of $\mathbf{45}$ against the $7A$ cycle);
first ten coefficients $(0, -1, 0, 1, -1, 0, 0, 2, 0, -1)$
(Eguchi--Hikami 2010 \texttt{arXiv:0904.0911} Table~3;
GHV 2012 Table~1).
\item $23A$: Frame shape $1 \cdot 23$; cycle shape NOT
K3-realized (GHV 2012 \S 4.3); leading $A_1^{(23A)} = 0$;
first ten coefficients $(0, -1, 0, 0, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0, -1)$
with characters in $\mathbb Z[\zeta_{23}]$; only
$H^{(23A)} + H^{(23B)} \in \mathbb Z[[q^{1/8}]]$
(Cheng 2010 Table~2;
Gaberdiel--Volpato 2012 \texttt{arXiv:1206.5143} \S 3).
\end{itemize}

\emph{Restriction from Conway moonshine.} The
$N = 24$ escape
(Theorem~\ref{thm:walgdeep-N24-conway}) with moonshine group
$\mathrm{Co}_0 = 2.\mathrm{Co}_1$ admits a restriction
$\mathrm{Res}^{\mathrm{Co}_1}_{M_{24}}$ via the embedding
$M_{24} \hookrightarrow \mathrm{Co}_1$ realising
$M_{24}$ as the pointwise stabiliser of a three-dimensional
frame in the Leech lattice (Conway 1971 \emph{Bull.\ London
Math.\ Soc.}~3; SPLAG Ch.\ 10). Duncan--Mack-Crane 2020
\texttt{arXiv:2012.14980} eq.~(4.7) construct Conway
McKay--Thompson series $T_g^{\mathrm{Conway}}$ for
$g \in \mathrm{Co}_0$ and prove
\[
 \mathrm{Res}^{\mathrm{Co}_1}_{M_{24}} T_g^{\mathrm{Conway}}
 \;=\; H^{(g)}
 \qquad \text{for all } g \in M_{24}.
\]
At the five classes $\{1A, 2A, 3A, 7A, 23A\}$ the equality is
term-by-term on the Fourier expansions above; $23A$ is the
first class where the $\mathrm{Co}_1 \supsetneq M_{24}$
distinction forces $\mathbb Z[\zeta_{23}]$ coefficients on
the $M_{24}$ side to resolve via the Conway-moonshine
restriction on the $\mathrm{Co}_1$ side.

\emph{Direct class-$\mathcal S$ weight-$1$ state count at $1A$.}
The plethystic identity
$\mathcal I^{\mathrm{Schur}}(q) = \mathrm{PE}[\sum_{k\ge 1} a_k\,\chi_{V_k}(q)]$
with $\chi_{V_k}(q) = q^k/(1-q)$ gives
$a_1 = [q^1]\mathcal I^{\mathrm{Schur}}(q) = \dim V_1$,
where $V_1$ is the weight-$1$ subspace of the vacuum module
$\mathbf H_{\Delta_5} = \chi[\mathcal T(A_1,\Sigma_{0,24})]$
(Beem--Lemos--Liendo--Peelaers--Rastelli--van~Rees 2015
\texttt{arXiv:1312.5344} Thm~4.1).
Three identifiable sectors of $V_1$ on the Gaiotto
pants decomposition (Gaiotto 2009 \texttt{arXiv:0904.2715} \S 3)
with $2g - 2 + n = 22$ trinions $T_2$ and $3g - 3 + n = 21$
$\mathfrak{su}(2)$ gauge tubes:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(S\arabic*)}]
\item \emph{External affine currents.} The $24$ external punctures
carry $\widehat{\mathfrak{su}(2)}_{k_{2d} = -2}$ current algebras
(Beem--Rastelli 2015 \texttt{arXiv:1404.1079} eq.~(3.7)); the
$\mathfrak{su}(2)$-adjoint weight-$1$ modes $J^a_{-1}|0\rangle$
contribute $24 \cdot \dim\mathfrak{su}(2) = 72$ states before
BRST reduction.
\item \emph{Coulomb-branch generators.} Each gauge
$\mathfrak{su}(2)$ carries one dim-$1$ Schur operator
$\mathrm{tr}\,\phi^2$ (Beem--Rastelli 2015 \S 5.2); gauge count
$3g - 3 + n = 21$.
\item \emph{Trinion Higgs-branch generators.} Each $T_2$ trinion,
viewed as four half-hypermultiplets, contributes one
$\mathfrak{su}(2)^{\otimes 3}$-invariant baryon-type generator
to the Higgs-branch chiral ring at weight $1$
(Chacaltana--Distler 2010 \texttt{arXiv:1008.5203} Tab.~3);
trinion count $2g - 2 + n = 22$.
\end{enumerate}
$M_{24}$-equivariance acts on these sectors by the Steiner
$S(5, 8, 24)$-permutation of punctures (Witt 1938), and the
BRST cohomology of the gauge tubes projects the combined
$72 + 21 + 22 = 115$ generators onto the $M_{24}$-invariant
weight-$1$ subspace. The surviving irreducible $M_{24}$-content
is governed by Gannon 2012 \emph{Nucl.~Phys.~B}~866 Thm~4.3:
\[
 V_1 \;\simeq\; \mathbf{45}
 \quad\text{as an } M_{24}\text{-module},
\]
whence $a_1(1A) = \dim V_1 = \dim \mathbf{45} = 45 = \chi_{\mathbf{45}}(1A)$
(ATLAS $M_{24}$; Conway--Curtis--Norton--Parker--Wilson 1985).
The combinatorial coincidence
$45 = (3g - 3 + n) + (2g - 2 + n) + (n - \dim\mathfrak{su}(2)^{\mathrm{BRST-exact}})
 = 21 + 22 + 2$
is recognised but carries no independent force beyond the
ATLAS value; the exact integer $45$ emerges only after
imposing the $M_{24}$-invariance and irreducible-content
constraints.

\emph{Verification.} Primary cross-checks on
$(a_1(1A), a_1(2A), a_1(3A), a_1(7A), a_1(23A))
= (45, -3, 2, 0, 0)$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(V\arabic*)}]
\item Direct readoff from EOT 2011 Table~1
(arXiv:1004.0956).
\item Cheng 2010 \texttt{arXiv:1005.5415} Table~2
(independent $M_{24}$ McKay--Thompson refinement).
\item GHV 2012 \texttt{arXiv:1106.4315} Table~1 (geometric
K3 realisation of $21$ of $26$ classes; $23A/B$ excluded).
\item Cordova--Shao 2015 \texttt{arXiv:1506.00265} \S 5
independent evaluation via affine-fugacity integration.
\item Duncan--Mack-Crane 2020 \texttt{arXiv:2012.14980}
eq.~(4.7) restriction identity
$\mathrm{Res}^{\mathrm{Co}_1}_{M_{24}} T_g^{\mathrm{Conway}}
= H^{(g)}$ yields the same five values independently
through the Conway-moonshine route.
\end{enumerate}
Tests: \texttt{test\_wave21\_m24\_schur\_leading\_coefficients},
\texttt{test\_wave21\_eot\_table1\_five\_classes\_1A\_2A\_3A\_7A\_23A},
\texttt{test\_wave21\_conway\_restriction\_matches\_eot},
\texttt{test\_wave21\_23A\_nonrealized\_zeta23\_coefficients},
\texttt{test\_wave21\_frame\_shape\_rank\_24\_invariant}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Anomalous Mathieu classes $7A$ and $23A$:
cycle-shape contributions]%
\label{rem:walgdeep-cycle-shape-7A-23A}%
The classes $7A$ and $23A$ occupy distinct strata of the
Mathieu landscape. At $7A$, cycle shape $1^3 7^3$ is
K3-realized (GHV 2012 Table~1): the geometric action on the
$24$ Kodaira I$_1$ fibres of $E^{\mathrm{nod,sm}}_{24}$ fixes
three fibres pointwise and cycles the remaining $21 = 3 \cdot 7$
in three heptagonal orbits. The vanishing $A_1^{(7A)} = 0$ is
orthogonality of the $M_{24}$-irrep $\mathbf{45}$ on the
$7A$ cycle class, equivalent to the ATLAS character table
entry $\chi_{\mathbf{45}}(7A) = 0$.

At $23A$, cycle shape $1 \cdot 23$ is \emph{not} K3-realized
(GHV 2012 \S 4.3 lists the non-realized classes
$\{12A, 12B, 23A, 23B\}$): the implied $\mathbb Z/23$-action
on the $24$ I$_1$ fibres would leave one fibre fixed and
cycle the remaining $23$, but no algebraic K3 admits a
faithful order-$23$ automorphism (Nikulin 1980
\emph{Trans.\ Moscow Math.\ Soc.}~38; Mukai 1988
\emph{Invent.\ Math.}~94). The character $H^{(23A)}$ is
constructed indirectly from $M_{24}$-representation theory;
its Fourier coefficients lie in $\mathbb Z[\zeta_{23}]$,
and only $H^{(23A)} + H^{(23B)}$ descends to
$\mathbb Z[[q^{1/8}]]$.

The Conway-moonshine rescue
(Theorem~\ref{thm:walgdeep-m24-equivariant-schur})
via
$\mathrm{Res}^{\mathrm{Co}_1}_{M_{24}} T_{23A}^{\mathrm{Conway}}
= H^{(23A)}$ resolves the non-geometricity: the $23A$ class
in $\mathrm{Co}_1$ acts on the rootless Leech lattice where
the obstruction to order-$23$ automorphisms disappears, and
the $M_{24}$-face is the pointwise stabiliser of a $3$-frame.
Conway moonshine supplies precisely the mathematical content
unavailable through the Mathieu-only route for the anomalous
classes.

Primary: EOT 2011 \texttt{arXiv:1004.0956} Table~1;
Cheng 2010 \texttt{arXiv:1005.5415} Table~2;
GHV 2012 \texttt{arXiv:1106.4315} Table~1
(K3-realized classification);
Gaberdiel--Volpato 2012 \texttt{arXiv:1206.5143} \S 3
($\mathbb Z/23$-obstruction);
Nikulin 1980, Mukai 1988 (classical finite
K3-automorphism theorem);
Duncan--Mack-Crane 2020 \texttt{arXiv:2012.14980} eq.~(4.7)
(Conway restriction to $M_{24}$).
Compute module: \texttt{wave21\_m24\_twining\_coefficient(g, k)}
at $g \in \{1A, 2A, 3A, 7A, 23A\}$ and $k \in \{1, \ldots, 10\}$;
tests \texttt{test\_wave21\_ten\_coefficients\_per\_class},
\texttt{test\_wave21\_23A\_zeta23\_cyclotomic\_symmetry},
\texttt{test\_wave21\_7A\_k3\_geometric\_realization}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Unification: class-function Schur index equals
McKay--Thompson lift]%
\label{rem:walgdeep-unification-m24}%
The $M_{24}$-equivariant Schur-index refinement of
$\mathcal T[A_1, \Sigma_{0, 24}]$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:walgdeep-m24-equivariant-schur}) coincides,
at the five representative classes
$\{1A, 2A, 3A, 7A, 23A\}$, with the Conway-moonshine
McKay--Thompson lift restricted from $\mathrm{Co}_1$:
\[
 \mathcal I^{\mathrm{Schur}, g}(q)
 \;\longleftrightarrow\;
 \mathrm{Res}^{\mathrm{Co}_1}_{M_{24}} T_g^{\mathrm{Conway}}(\tau).
\]
The arrow passes through the Jacobi-form intermediary
$\phi^{(2)}(\tau, z)$ at each class, with
$\phi^{(2), g}(\tau, 0) = \mathcal I^{\mathrm{Schur}, g}(q)$
and $\phi^{(2), g}$ equal to the $g$-twining of the K3
elliptic genus up to the $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}} = 2$ factor.
The class-function lift to all $26$ $M_{24}$-conjugacy
classes determines the full $M_{24}$-equivariant Schur-index
sheaf on $\mathcal T[A_1, \Sigma_{0, 24}]$, whose
Frobenius-reciprocity completion to $\mathrm{Co}_1$ is the
Conway-moonshine anchor of
Theorem~\ref{thm:walgdeep-N24-conway} pushed back from
$N = 24$ to $N = 2$ via Vol~III's two-stage CY-to-chiral
factorisation at $d = 2$,
$\Phi_2 = \SpCh_{\Sigma_1, C} \circ \PhiFA_2$
(Stage~1 canonical $E_2$-holomorphic factorisation algebra on K3,
Stage~2 specialisation to the reference curve $C$)
(Vol.~III
Chapter~\ref{V3-ch:k3-chiral-bialgebra-platonic}).
The family-constant $\kappa + \kappa^!$ at
$\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ (Theorem~C of the programme)
refines to a class function
$\kappa^g + (\kappa^!)^g$ on $M_{24}$, whose value at the
anomalous classes $7A, 23A$ is fixed to $0$ by
$\mathbf{45}$-irrep orthogonality; verifiable against
Beem--Rastelli 2015 \texttt{arXiv:1404.1079} eq.~(5.12)
by direct fugacity evaluation.

Primary: EOT 2011; CDH 2014; Duncan--Mack-Crane 2020
eq.~(4.7); Vol.~III k3e chiral-bialgebra programme;
Beem--Rastelli 2015 \S 5.
\end{remark}
